* **System Abolished:** The complex "Double Government" system introduced by **Pitt‚Äôs India Act (1784)**‚Äîwhich split power between the *Court of Directors* (Company) and the *Board of Control* (Government)‚Äîwas scrapped.
* **New Authority:** All their powers were unified and vested in a new cabinet minister position in the British Parliament.

### 3. New Office: Secretary of State for India

* **The Position:** A new high-ranking minister, the **Secretary of State for India**, was appointed. He was a member of the British Cabinet and was responsible to the British Parliament.
* **The Council:** To assist him, a **Council of India** was established, consisting of **15 members**. This was an advisory body, and the Secretary of State was its Chairman.

### 4. Governor-General becomes "Viceroy"

* **Change in Title:** The designation of the head of administration in India was changed from *Governor-General of India* to **Viceroy of India**.
* **Role:** He became the direct representative of the British Crown in India.
* **First Viceroy:** **Lord Canning** (who was the Governor-General during the 1857 revolt) became the first Viceroy.

---

# üìú The Queen's Proclamation (1858)

*The Magna Carta of the Indian People*

On **November 1, 1858**, at a grand Durbar in Allahabad, Lord Canning read out the Royal Proclamation issued by Queen Victoria. It laid down the principles of the new rule:

1. **No More Annexation:** The era of expansion was declared over. The British promised not to seek further territorial expansion in India (effectively ending the *Doctrine of Lapse*).
2. **Respect for Princely States:** The treaties and rights of Indian Princes were to be honored. The Princes were now allies, not enemies.
3. **Religious Non-Interference:** The British government promised not to interfere in the ancient religious beliefs and customs of the people.
4. **Equal Protection:** All Indians would be treated equally under the law, regardless of race or creed.
5. **Access to Service:** Indians would be admitted to offices in the government service based on education and ability, "freely and impartially."

---

### ‚öñÔ∏è Summary of the Shift

| Feature | **Before 1858 (Company Rule)** | **After 1858 (Crown Rule)** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Source of Power** | East India Company (Charter) | British Parliament / Crown |
| **Top Official in London** | President of Board of Control | **Secretary of State for India** |
| **Top Official in India** | Governor-General | **Viceroy** |
| **Administration** | Double Government (Directors + Board) | Direct Administration (Sec. of State + Council) |
| **Policy Stance** | Aggressive Expansion (Dalhousie) | Status Quo & "Good Government" |



Here is a detailed breakdown of the **Revolt of 1857**, often called India‚Äôs "First War of Independence."

---

# üî• The Revolt of 1857: The Great Uprising

> *"In this instance we could not play off the Mohammedans against the Hindus."* ‚Äî **Aitchison** (A British Official lamenting the Hindu-Muslim unity during the revolt).

The Revolt was the culmination of a century of British exploitation. It was not a sudden event but a volcano that had been simmering for decades.

---

## üí£ I. Causes of the Revolt

The causes were a complex mix of political, economic, socio-religious, and military grievances.

### 1. Political Causes (The Fear of Annexation)

* **Doctrine of Lapse:** Lord Dalhousie‚Äôs aggressive policy annexed states like **Satara, Jhansi, and Nagpur** because the rulers had no natural heir.
* **Annexation of Awadh (1856):** Awadh was annexed on the grounds of "misgovernance," leaving thousands of nobles, officials, and soldiers unemployed.
* **Disrespect to Mughals:** Lord Canning announced that after Bahadur Shah Zafar, the Mughals would lose the title of "King" and have to move out of the Red Fort.

### 2. Economic Causes (Destruction of Livelihood)

* **Heavy Taxation:** Peasants were overburdened by the Zamindari and Ryotwari systems.
* **De-industrialization:** British trade policies destroyed Indian handicrafts (textiles, pottery), turning artisans into landless laborers.

### 3. Socio-Religious Causes (Threat to Dharma)

* **Social Reforms:** Laws banning **Sati (1829)** and allowing **Widow Remarriage (1856)** were seen by orthodox Indians as interference in their religion.
* **Missionary Activity:** The aggressive spread of Christianity and the *Religious Disabilities Act (1850)* (which allowed Christian converts to inherit ancestral property) created fear of mass conversion.

### 4. Military Causes (Sepoy Discontent)

* **General Service Enlistment Act (1856):** Mandated that sepoys must serve overseas if required. In Hinduism, crossing the sea (*Kala Pani*) meant losing one's caste.
* **Discrimination:** Indian soldiers were paid less than Europeans and could not rise above the rank of *Subedar*.

### 5. The Immediate Cause (The Spark)

* **The Enfield Rifle:** A new rifle was introduced where the cartridges had to be bitten off before loading. Rumors spread that the grease was made of **Cow and Pig fat**.
* This offended both Hindus (Cow is sacred) and Muslims (Pig is haram).


* **Mangal Pandey:** On **March 29, 1857**, at Barrackpore, Mangal Pandey refused to use the cartridge and attacked his officers. He was hanged, becoming the first martyr.

---

## üö© II. Centers & Leaders of the Revolt

The revolt formally began on **May 10, 1857**, when sepoys at **Meerut** mutinied and marched to Delhi.

| **Center** | **Key Leader** | **Notes** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Delhi** | **Bahadur Shah Zafar** | The symbolic head. Real command was with **General Bakht Khan**. |
| **Kanpur** | **Nana Saheb** | Adopted son of Peshwa Baji Rao II (denied pension). Assisted by **Tantia Tope**. |
| **Lucknow** | **Begum Hazrat Mahal** | Wife of the deposed Nawab of Awadh. She refused to surrender and eventually escaped to Nepal. |
| **Jhansi** | **Rani Laxmibai** | Fought against the Doctrine of Lapse. Famous for dying in battle dressed as a man. *"Main apni Jhansi nahi dungi."* |
| **Bihar (Arrah)** | **Kunwar Singh** | An 80-year-old Zamindar who arguably had the best military record in the revolt. |
| **Faizabad** | **Maulvi Ahmadullah** | A Madrasa teacher who fought stiff battles; the British put a bounty on his head. |

---

## ‚öîÔ∏è III. Suppression of the Revolt

The British ruthlessly suppressed the revolt using superior resources and technology (Telegraph).

* **Delhi (Sept 1857):** Recaptured by **John Nicholson**. Bahadur Shah Zafar was arrested and exiled to Rangoon (Burma), where he died in 1862. His sons were shot dead.
* **Kanpur (Dec 1857):** Recaptured by **Colin Campbell**. Nana Saheb escaped to Nepal. Tantia Tope fought a guerilla war until he was betrayed and hanged in 1859.
* **Jhansi (June 1858):** Captured by **Sir Hugh Rose**. Rani Laxmibai died fighting in Gwalior.
* *Hugh Rose's Tribute:* "Here lay the woman who was the only man among the rebels."


* **Lucknow (March 1858):** Recaptured by Colin Campbell.

---

## ‚ùì IV. Nature of the Revolt

Historians are divided on what to call this event:

1. **Sepoy Mutiny:** British historians (like Sir John Lawrence) called it a mere military mutiny of the sepoys.
2. **First War of Independence:** **V.D. Savarkar** described it as the first organized national struggle for freedom.
3. **Feudal Outburst:** Marxist historians call it a struggle of the old feudal order (Kings/Zamindars) trying to regain their lost power.
4. **R.C. Majumdar‚Äôs View:** *"It was neither the first, nor national, nor a war of independence"* (arguing that "nationalism" didn't exist yet).

---

## üìâ V. Consequences of the Revolt

Though the revolt failed militarily, it forced the British to completely overhaul their administration.

1. **End of Company Rule:** The **Government of India Act 1858** transferred power from the East India Company to the **British Crown**.
2. **Queen's Proclamation:** Promised non-interference in religious affairs and no further annexation of Princely States.
3. **Army Reorganization (Peel Commission):**
* The proportion of Europeans to Indians in the army was increased (to prevent future mutinies).
* Artillery was placed exclusively in European hands.
* "Martial Races" (Sikhs, Gurkhas, Pathans) who had supported the British were recruited more, while soldiers from Awadh/Bengal were reduced.


4. **Divide and Rule:** The British concluded that Hindu-Muslim unity was dangerous. They began a conscious policy of creating a rift between the communities.


 **Growth of Nationalism in India (1858‚Äì1905)**, describing how a fragmented subcontinent transformed into a nation with a unified political voice.

---

# üáÆüá≥ The Genesis of a Nation (1858‚Äì1905)

Post-1857, the direct rule of the British Crown unwittingly sowed the seeds of Indian nationalism. The very tools used to colonize India‚Äîrailways, English education, and administrative unity‚Äîbecame the tools used to liberate it.

---

## üîó 1. Political, Economic & Administrative Unification

For the first time in history, the entire Indian subcontinent (from the Himalayas to Kanyakumari) was under a single authority.

* **Administrative Unity:** The British created a highly centralized state with a uniform system of law (*Indian Penal Code*), a single currency, and a professional **Civil Service (ICS)**. This created a sense of "pan-Indian" citizenship.
* **Communication Network:**
* **Railways:** Introduced in 1853, railways broke down geographical barriers, allowing a Bengali intellectual to meet a Maratha leader.
* **Telegraph & Post:** Enabled rapid exchange of political ideas across vast distances.


* **Economic Unification:** The destruction of rural self-sufficiency meant that a famine in Odisha affected prices in Madras. This economic interdependence made Indians realize they shared a common economic destiny (and a common enemy).

---

## üéì 2. Role of Western Education

The introduction of modern education (Macaulay‚Äôs Minute, 1835) was meant to create "clerks," but it ended up creating "nationalists."

* **Window to the West:** Educated Indians read European thinkers like **John Stuart Mill, Rousseau, and Spencer**. They absorbed modern concepts of *Liberty, Equality, Democracy, and Sovereignty*.
* **Lingua Franca:** With hundreds of dialects in India, **English** became the common language of the intelligentsia. A Tamil lawyer could now debate with a Punjabi journalist in a shared language.
* **The Middle Class:** It gave rise to a new professional middle class (lawyers, doctors, teachers) who provided leadership to the national movement (e.g., Gandhi, Nehru, Bose were all Western-educated).

---

## üì∞ 3. Role of the Press

The press became the "Parliament" of the people in the absence of a real legislature.

* **The Vernacular Voice:** Regional newspapers like *Amrita Bazar Patrika* (Bengali), *Kesari* (Marathi), and *The Hindu* (English/Tamil region) critiqued British policies relentlessly.
* **Political Education:** They exposed colonial exploitation (e.g., covering famines and indentured labor) and fostered a feeling of national solidarity.
* **Library Movement:** Newspapers were often read aloud in local libraries, reaching even the illiterate masses.

> **Key Reaction:** Fearing this power, Lord Lytton passed the **Vernacular Press Act (1878)** to gag Indian language papers, but this only fueled more anger.

---

## üèõÔ∏è 4. Rediscovery of India‚Äôs Past

Colonial rulers often justified their rule by claiming Indians were "uncivilized" and needed the "White Man's Burden." This myth was shattered by scholars.

* **The Orientalists:** European scholars like **Max Mueller**, **William Jones**, and **Alexander Cunningham** (ASI) deciphered ancient texts and inscriptions.
* **Restoring Pride:** Indians learned that their ancestors had built the Indus Valley Civilization, written the Vedas, and formulated advanced mathematics (Aryabhata) when Europe was in the Dark Ages.
* **Impact:** This psychological boost gave leaders like **Swami Vivekananda** and **Dayanand Saraswati** the confidence to preach that Indians were capable of self-rule (*Swaraj*).

---

## üì¢ 5. Early Political Movements (Pre-Congress)

Before the Indian National Congress (INC), political activity was regional and elite-led.

| Year | Organization | Founder/Leader | Region | Significance |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **1838** | **Landholders' Society** | Dwarkanath Tagore | Bengal | First organized political group; defended Zamindar interests. |
| **1866** | **East India Association** | **Dadabhai Naoroji** | London | Aimed to influence British public opinion about India. |
| **1876** | **Indian Association** | **Surendranath Banerjee** | Bengal | The first **mass organization**. Agitated against the reduction of age limit for Civil Services. |
| **1884** | **Madras Mahajan Sabha** | Viraraghavachari | Madras | Focused on local administrative reforms. |
| **1885** | **Bombay Presidency Assoc.** | Pherozeshah Mehta | Bombay | Political activism in Western India. |

---

## ü§ù 6. Formation of the Indian National Congress (1885)

The need for an all-India body culminated in the birth of the Congress.

* **The Founder:** **Allan Octavian Hume** (a retired British Civil Servant) mobilized Indian leaders.
* **First Session (1885):**
* **Venue:** Gokuldas Tejpal Sanskrit College, **Bombay**.
* **President:** **W.C. Bonnerjee**.
* **Attendees:** 72 delegates (mostly lawyers, journalists, and teachers).


* **The "Safety Valve" Theory:** Many historians (and extremists like Lala Lajpat Rai) believed Hume formed the INC to provide a peaceful outlet ("safety valve") for growing Indian discontent, preventing another violent revolt like 1857.

---

## ‚öñÔ∏è 7. Era of Moderates (1885‚Äì1905)

The first phase of the Congress was dominated by leaders who believed in the British sense of justice and fair play.

* **Key Leaders:** **Dadabhai Naoroji** (Grand Old Man of India), **Gopal Krishna Gokhale** (Gandhi's Guru), **Pherozeshah Mehta**.
* **Methodology (The 3 Ps):**
1. **P**rayer
2. **P**etition
3. **P**rotest (Constitutional agitation within the law).


* **Demands:**
* **"No Taxation without Representation."**
* Expansion of Legislative Councils.
* Indianization of the Civil Services (ICS).
* Reduction of military expenditure.



### **Major Achievements of Moderates:**

1. **Economic Critique:** Dadabhai Naoroji propounded the **"Drain of Wealth" Theory** in his book *Poverty and Un-British Rule in India*, mathematically proving that Britain was bleeding India dry. This destroyed the moral authority of British rule.
2. **Indian Councils Act 1892:** Forced the British to expand the size of legislative councils and allow indirect elections (a small victory for democracy).
3. **Public Awareness:** They trained Indians in the art of political work and created a national awakening.

### **Limitations:**

* They were an elite club; they failed to connect with the masses (peasants, workers).
* They were criticized as "political mendicants" (beggars) by the younger generation (Extremists) for their soft approach.

---

detailed breakdown of the **Swadeshi Movement (1905)**, often regarded as the rehearsal for the mass movements of the Gandhian era.

---

# üêÖ The Swadeshi Movement (1905‚Äì1908)

*The First Roar of Mass Nationalism*

> *"The partition of Bengal is a settled fact."* ‚Äî **Lord Curzon**
> *"We shall unsettle the settled fact."* ‚Äî **Surendranath Banerjee**

The Swadeshi Movement was the first successful mass movement in Indian history. It transformed the Indian National Congress from a club of lawyers into a vehicle for public outrage.

---

## üî™ 1. The Trigger: The Partition of Bengal

In 1903, the British announced plans to divide Bengal. The official partition came into force on **October 16, 1905**.

### **A. The Logic of Partition**

* **Official Reason:** "Administrative Efficiency." Bengal was huge (Population: 78 Million, including Bihar and Odisha) and difficult to manage.
* **Real Reason (Divide & Rule):** To split the Bengali-speaking population, which was the nerve center of Indian nationalism.
* **Linguistic Split:** Bengalis would become a minority in their own province (outnumbered by Hindi/Odia speakers in the West).
* **Religious Split:** West Bengal was Hindu-majority; East Bengal & Assam was Muslim-majority. Curzon openly courted Muslims, promising them a "revived Mughal glory" in Dhaka.



### **B. Day of Partition (Oct 16, 1905)**

The day was observed as a **Day of Mourning**.

* **Raksha Bandhan:** Rabindranath Tagore called for Hindus and Muslims to tie Rakhis on each other's wrists to symbolize unity.
* **Arandhan:** No fires were lit in kitchens (cooking strike).
* **Vande Mataram:** Overnight, Bankim Chandra Chatterjee‚Äôs song became the national war cry.

---

## ‚úä 2. The Twin Weapons: Swadeshi & Boycott

The movement had two distinct faces: *Negative* (Boycott) and *Positive* (Swadeshi).

### **A. The Boycott (The Weapon of Destruction)**

* **Bonfires:** Massive bonfires of Manchester cloth were lit at street corners.
* **Social Ostracism:** Those selling or using foreign goods were socially boycotted. Washermen refused to wash foreign clothes; priests refused to perform rituals with foreign sugar or items.
* **Picketing:** Students and women stood outside shops selling foreign goods, blocking entry.

### **B. Swadeshi (The Weapon of Creation)**

"Swadeshi" meant self-reliance (*Atma-Shakti*). If India boycotted British goods, it had to produce its own.

* **Industry:** Indigenous factories sprang up.
* *Acharya P.C. Ray* set up **Bengal Chemicals**.
* *J.N. Tata* laid the groundwork for the Tata Iron and Steel Company (TISCO).
* Swadeshi banks and insurance companies were founded.


* **Education:** Students were expelled for shouting "Vande Mataram." To support them, the **National Council of Education** (1906) was set up.
* *Aurobindo Ghosh* became the principal of the Bengal National College.


* **Culture:**
* *Tagore* wrote "Amar Sonar Bangla" (My Golden Bengal).
* *Abanindranath Tagore* painted "Bharat Mata," depicting the nation as a mother goddess.



---

## üó£Ô∏è 3. Methods of Mass Mobilization

The movement innovated new ways to reach the illiterate masses.

1. **The Samitis (Volunteer Corps):** These were the backbone of the movement.
* *Swadesh Bandhab Samiti* (Barisal): Led by **Ashwini Kumar Dutta**, it had 159 branches and mobilized Muslim peasants.
* *Anushilan Samiti* (Calcutta): Focused on physical training and revolutionary ideas.


2. **Festivals as Platforms:** **Bal Gangadhar Tilak** used the **Ganapati** and **Shivaji** festivals in Maharashtra to preach nationalism, bypassing the ban on political meetings.
3. **Folk Theatre (Jatra):** Traditional folk forms were used to spread political messages in villages.

---

## üë• 4. Social Base: Who Joined?

| Group | Participation Level | Role |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Students** | **Very High** | The foot soldiers. They picketed shops and spread the message. |
| **Women** | **Significant** | For the first time, middle-class women stepped out of their homes to join processions and picketing. |
| **Zamindars** | **High** | Many big Zamindars joined the movement (unlike in 1857), creating a united front against the British. |
| **Muslims** | **Mixed** | Middle-class Muslims joined, but the British successfully alienated the Muslim peasantry by calling Swadeshi a "Hindu" movement. |
| **Labor** | **Emerging** | Strikes occurred in the railways and jute mills, marking the birth of the Indian trade union movement. |

---

## üèõÔ∏è 5. The Surat Split (1907): The Movement Fractures

The movement intensified the ideological battle within the Congress between:

* **Moderates (Gokhale, Pherozeshah Mehta):** Wanted to restrict the Boycott to Bengal and use constitutional methods.
* **Extremists (Lal-Bal-Pal):** Wanted to extend the movement to the whole of India and aim for **Swaraj** (Self-rule).

This tension led to the **Surat Split (1907)**, where the Congress broke into two. The British used this weakness to crack down heavily.

---

## üìâ 6. Decline and Annulment

By 1908, the movement fizzled out.

* **Repression:** Tilak was jailed (1908), Aurobindo Ghosh retired to an ashram in Pondicherry, and Bipin Chandra Pal left politics.
* **Lack of Organization:** The movement was leaderless and lacked a disciplined party structure (unlike the later Gandhian movements).

### **The Victory (1911)**

However, the pressure worked. To prevent further unrest, the British government announced at the **Delhi Durbar (1911)**:

1. **The Partition was annulled.** Bengal was reunited.
2. **Capital Shift:** The capital of India was moved from Calcutta to **Delhi** (a safer, more central location away from the "troublesome" Bengalis).

### üìù Significance

1. **Cultural Awakening:** It proved India could be self-reliant in industry and education.
2. **Mass Politics:** It took politics from the drawing rooms of the elite to the streets.
3. **Goal Set:** The demand shifted from "Reform" to "Swaraj."

---

the **Extremist Phase (1905‚Äì1917)** of the Indian National Movement, a period that shifted the gear from "Petition" to "Protest."

---

# üî• The Era of Militant Nationalism (The Extremist Phase)

> *"Swaraj is my birthright and I shall have it."* ‚Äî **Bal Gangadhar Tilak**

Between 1905 and 1917, the Indian National Congress witnessed a tectonic shift. A new group of leaders emerged who believed that the British would not leave out of benevolence; they had to be pushed out by force of will and mass action.

---

## üßê I. Why did Extremism Rise?

The rise of the Extremists was not accidental. It was a reaction to the failure of the "Moderate" methods.

1. **Failure of the Moderates:** After 20 years of "Prayer, Petition, and Protest," the British had given almost nothing. The younger generation felt that the Moderates were "political mendicants" (beggars).
2. **The Curzon Shock:** Lord Curzon‚Äôs reactionary policies‚Äîlimiting higher education (*Universities Act 1904*), curbing the press, and finally the **Partition of Bengal (1905)**‚Äîproved that the British had no intention of being fair.
3. **International Inspiration:**
* **Ethiopia defeated Italy (1896).**
* **Japan defeated Russia (1905).**
* These wars shattered the myth of "European invincibility." If Asian Japan could beat European Russia, why couldn't India beat Britain?


4. **Worsening Economic Conditions:** Famines were frequent, and plague was rampant (especially in Pune), yet the British celebrated the Grand Durbar of 1903.

---

## ü¶Å II. The Pillars of Extremism (Lal-Bal-Pal)

The movement was led by a trinity of leaders representing three different regions, united by one ideology.

| Leader | Region | Contribution & Style |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Bal Gangadhar Tilak** | **Maharashtra** | The "Father of Indian Unrest." He transformed the **Ganapati** and **Shivaji** festivals into political rallies. He ran the newspapers *Kesari* (Marathi) and *Mahratta* (English). |
| **Lala Lajpat Rai** | **Punjab** | "Sher-e-Punjab" (Lion of Punjab). He focused on Swadeshi and suffered police brutality during the Simon Commission protest later. |
| **Bipin Chandra Pal** | **Bengal** | The orator and theoretician. He argued that political freedom was the first step toward spiritual and social progress. |
| **Aurobindo Ghosh** | **Bengal** | The intellectual powerhouse. He advocated **"Passive Resistance"**‚Äîorganized refusal to pay taxes or obey unjust laws. |

---

## ‚öîÔ∏è III. Ideology: How were they different?

The core difference lay in the *Goal* and the *Method*.

| Feature | **Moderates (1885‚Äì1905)** | **Extremists (1905‚Äì1917)** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Goal** | **Dominion Status** (Self-rule *within* the British Empire, like Canada). | **Swaraj** (Complete Self-Rule). |
| **Method** | Constitutional agitation (Petitions, Meetings, Resolutions). | **Direct Action** (Strikes, Boycott, Mass mobilization). |
| **Base** | Urban Intelligentsia (Lawyers, Elites). | Middle class, Students, Women, Lower middle class. |
| **Faith** | Believed in the British sense of justice. | Believed the British were exploiters. |

---

## ‚ö° IV. Key Events of the Phase

### 1. The Surat Split (1907)

*The Great Divorce*
The tension between Moderates and Extremists exploded at the Congress Session in Surat.

* **The Spark:** The Extremists wanted Tilak to be President. The Moderates (led by Pherozeshah Mehta) manipulated the rules to elect Rash Behari Ghosh.
* **The Climax:** A shoe was thrown at the dais. The meeting turned into a brawl.
* **The Result:** The Extremists were **expelled** from the Congress. The British government immediately arrested Tilak (sent to Mandalay Jail, Burma for 6 years) and arrested Aurobindo Ghosh.

### 2. The Wilderness Years (1908‚Äì1914)

With Tilak in jail and Aurobindo retired to an Ashram in Pondicherry, the national movement slumped. The Moderates controlled the Congress but had no popular support.

### 3. The Lucknow Pact (1916)

*The Reunion*
The movement revived during World War I.

* **Reunion:** Tilak returned from jail, and the Moderates realized they were powerless without the masses. The two wings reunited at the Lucknow Session.
* **Hindu-Muslim Unity:** The Congress and the **Muslim League** (led by Jinnah) signed a pact to demand self-government together.

### 4. Home Rule League Movement (1916)

Since the Congress was still sluggish, Tilak and **Annie Besant** started separate Home Rule Leagues to keep the agitation alive.

* **Tilak‚Äôs League:** Focused on Maharashtra and Karnataka.
* **Besant‚Äôs League:** Focused on the rest of India.
* **Impact:** They set up a network of committees that Gandhi would later use for his mass movements.

---

## üìâ V. Why did it Decline?

1. **Government Repression:** The British passed the *Seditious Meetings Act (1907)* and the *Press Act (1910)* to crush dissent.
2. **Lack of Mass Structure:** While they mobilized crowds, they didn't have a disciplined party structure (which Gandhi later built).
3. **Ideological Limits:** Their emphasis on Hindu symbols (Ganapati, Shivaji, Goddess Kali) inadvertently alienated some Muslim peasants, allowing the British to play the "Divide and Rule" card.

### üìù Significance

The Extremists taught India "Self-Confidence." They destroyed the fear of authority and transformed patriotism from a "hobby" into a "full-time devotion."

---
the **Revolutionary Terrorism Phase I**, the fiery aftermath of the Swadeshi Movement's suppression.

---

# üí£ The Era of Revolutionary Heroism (Phase I: 1907‚Äì1917)

*Propaganda by Deed*

> *"We shall die to awaken the nation."* ‚Äî **Bagha Jatin**

When the open mass movement (Swadeshi) was brutally crushed and the political leaders (Tilak, Aurobindo) were jailed or exiled, the youth of India felt frustrated. Disillusioned with the "mendicancy" of the Moderates and the temporary failure of mass agitation, they turned to individual heroism.

**Their Philosophy:** If the British rule by the sword, they must be answered with the sword. The goal was to strike terror in the hearts of colonial officials to demoralize the administration.

---

## üìç 1. Bengal: The Cockpit of Revolution

Bengal was the nerve center. The revolutionaries here were deeply influenced by the novels of **Bankim Chandra Chatterjee** (*Anandamath*) and the teachings of **Swami Vivekananda**.

### **A. Key Organizations**

* **Anushilan Samiti (1902):** Founded by **Promotha Mitter**. Originally a physical training society, it secretly trained members in lathi-play and dagger usage.
* **Yugantar Group (1906):** An inner circle of the Anushilan Samiti led by **Barindra Kumar Ghosh** (Aurobindo‚Äôs brother) and **Bhupendranath Dutta**. They started the weekly newspaper *Yugantar*, which openly preached armed rebellion.

### **B. Major Incidents**

* **Attempt on Fuller (1906):** Failed attempt to kill Lt. Governor Fuller (who famously said he had "two wives, Hindu and Muslim, and the Muslim was the favorite").
* **The Alipore Bomb Case (1908):**
* **The Target:** Douglas Kingsford (a sadistic judge known for flogging Swadeshi activists).
* **The Action:** Two young revolutionaries, **Khudiram Bose** (18) and **Prafulla Chaki**, threw a bomb at a carriage in Muzaffarpur believing Kingsford was inside.
* **The Tragedy:** Kingsford was not in the carriage; two British ladies (Mrs. Kennedy and her daughter) were killed.
* **The Aftermath:** Prafulla Chaki committed suicide. Khudiram Bose was hanged (becoming a folk hero). Aurobindo Ghosh was arrested but acquitted (defended brilliantly by C.R. Das); he later retired to Pondicherry.


* **The "Zimmerman Plan" (1915):** Led by **Jatindranath Mukherjee (Bagha Jatin)**. It was a bold plan to receive German arms during WWI to launch a pan-India insurrection. The plan was betrayed. Bagha Jatin died fighting the British police in a trench battle at Balasore (Odisha).
* *Famous Quote:* "Amra morbo, jagat jagbe" (We shall die, the nation shall awake).



---

## üö© 2. Maharashtra: The Savarkar Legacy

Revolutionary ideas here were linked to the resurrection of Maratha pride.

* **Abhinav Bharat (1904):** A secret society founded by the **Savarkar Brothers** (Ganesh and Vinayak Damodar Savarkar). It was modeled on Mazzini's "Young Italy."
* **Nasik Conspiracy (1909):** **Anant Kanhare**, a member of Abhinav Bharat, shot dead **A.M.T. Jackson** (District Magistrate of Nasik) at a theatre.
* *Reason:* Jackson had deported Babarao Savarkar (Vinayak's brother).



---

## üåæ 3. Punjab: The Ghadar Movement

In Punjab, the movement was fueled by famine, land revenue increases, and the mistreatment of Indians abroad.

* **Assassination of Curzon Wyllie (1909):** **Madan Lal Dhingra** shot Wyllie (a British official) in London. Dhingra famously stated, *"The only lesson required in India at present is to learn how to die, and the only way to teach it is by dying ourselves."*
* **The Delhi Conspiracy (1912):** **Rash Behari Bose** and **Sachin Sanyal** threw a bomb at **Viceroy Lord Hardinge** while he was entering Delhi (during the capital transfer procession). Hardinge was injured, but survived. Rash Behari Bose managed to escape to Japan (where he later helped found the INA).

### **The Ghadar Party (1913)**

* **Location:** San Francisco, USA.
* **Founder:** **Lala Har Dayal**, Sohan Singh Bhakna.
* **Goal:** To organize a rebellion in India using Indian soldiers (sepoys) while Britain was distracted by World War I.
* **The Komagata Maru Incident (1914):**
* A Japanese ship chartered by Gurdit Singh carrying 376 Indians (mostly Sikhs) was turned away from Vancouver, Canada, due to racist laws.
* When the ship returned to India (Budge Budge, Calcutta), the British police tried to arrest the leaders. A riot ensued, and 22 people were killed.
* **Impact:** This enraged the Ghadarites, who launched a premature uprising in Punjab in 1915. It was crushed due to treachery, but it radicalized the Punjab region (laying the ground for Bhagat Singh later).



---

## üìâ Significance & Decline

* **Why it failed:** It was an elite movement. Individual acts of heroism could not mobilize the masses. The British police state was too strong for unorganized groups.
* **Legacy:** They banished the fear of the British from the minds of the people. They proved that Indians were willing to kill and die for freedom.

### üöÄ Next Step

The violent first phase ends around 1917. The vacuum is about to be filled by a very different kind of leader.



the **Socio-Religious Reform Movements** (19th‚Äì20th Century), popularly known as the "Indian Renaissance."

---

# üïØÔ∏è The Indian Renaissance: Socio-Religious Reform Movements

*Awakening the Sleeping Giant*

> *"I regret to say that the present system of religion adhered to by the Hindus is not well calculated to promote their political interest... it is, I think, necessary that some change should take place in their religion for the sake of their political advantage and social comfort."* ‚Äî **Raja Ram Mohan Roy**

Before India could fight for political freedom, it had to fight against its own social evils. The 19th century saw a wave of intellectual awakening aimed at purifying Indian society of Sati, untouchability, idolatry, and the suppression of women.

---

## üßê I. Why did these movements start?

1. **Social Obsolescence:** Society was riddled with rigid caste lines, untouchability, and female infanticide.
2. **Western Education:** Educated Indians began comparing their society with the rational, scientific, and humanistic values of the West.
3. **Christian Missionaries:** The aggressive conversion activities of missionaries forced Hinduism and Islam to "reform or perish."

---

## ‚öñÔ∏è II. Classification: Reformist vs. Revivalist

| **Reformist Movements** | **Revivalist Movements** |
| --- | --- |
| Attempted to change society using **Reason** and **Western Humanism**. | Attempted to change society by returning to **Ancient Purity**. |
| Believed in synthesis of East and West. | Believed Western culture was corrupting; "Go back to the roots." |
| **Examples:** Brahmo Samaj, Prarthana Samaj, Aligarh Movement. | **Examples:** Arya Samaj, Deoband Movement, Ramakrishna Mission. |

---

## üïâÔ∏è III. Major Hindu Reform Movements

### 1. Brahmo Samaj (The Reformist Pioneer)

* **Founder:** **Raja Ram Mohan Roy** (1828). Later led by **Debendranath Tagore** and **Keshub Chandra Sen**.
* **Region:** Bengal.
* **Philosophy:** **Monotheism** (One God). Rejected idol worship, Avatarism, and the caste system.
* **Key Achievement:** Their agitation led to the **Abolition of Sati Act (1829)** by Lord William Bentinck.

### 2. Arya Samaj (The Militant Revivalist)

* **Founder:** **Dayanand Saraswati** (1875).
* **Region:** North India (Punjab/UP).
* **Philosophy:** **"Go Back to the Vedas."**
* Believed the Vedas were infallible and contained all scientific truth.
* Rejected Puranas and idol worship.


* **Shuddhi Movement:** A controversial ritual to convert non-Hindus (or those who had converted to Islam/Christianity) back to Hinduism.
* **Education:** Founded the **DAV (Dayanand Anglo-Vedic) Schools** (modern education) and **Gurukuls** (traditional education).

### 3. Ramakrishna Mission (Spiritual Nationalism)

* **Founder:** **Swami Vivekananda** (1897), disciple of the mystic Ramakrishna Paramahansa.
* **Philosophy:** *"Daridra Narayana"* (Service to the poor is service to God).
* **Significance:** Vivekananda restored pride in Indian culture at the global stage (**Parliament of Religions, Chicago, 1893**). He argued that India needed "Muscles of Iron and Nerves of Steel," not just prayers.

### 4. Prarthana Samaj

* **Founder:** **Atmaram Pandurang** (1867) in Bombay; popularized by **M.G. Ranade**.
* **Focus:** Rational worship and social reform.
* **Agenda:** Disapproval of caste, widow remarriage, and women's education.

### 5. Young Bengal Movement

* **Leader:** **Henry Vivian Derozio** (Anglo-Indian teacher at Hindu College).
* **Nature:** Radical and intellectual. Inspired by the **French Revolution**.
* **Outcome:** They attacked old traditions too aggressively (eating beef, drinking wine) and failed to connect with the masses, but inspired critical thinking.

---

## ‚ò™Ô∏è IV. Muslim Reform Movements

The Muslim community, having lost political power to the British, initially withdrew into a shell. Two opposing movements emerged to uplift them.

### 1. Aligarh Movement (Reformist)

* **Leader:** **Sir Syed Ahmed Khan**.
* **Philosophy:** The Quran must be interpreted in the light of modern science and reason.
* **Goal:** To reconcile Muslims with British rule and modern education.
* **Achievement:** Founded the **Mohammedan Anglo-Oriental College (1875)**, which later became **Aligarh Muslim University (AMU)**.

### 2. Deoband Movement (Revivalist)

* **Leaders:** Mohammad Qasim Nanautavi and Rashid Ahmed Gangohi (1866).
* **Philosophy:** Orthodox Islam. Issued *Fatwas* against British culture.
* **Goal:** To purify Islam of foreign elements and promote Jihad against foreign rule. (Opposed the Aligarh movement).

---

## ‚úä V. Caste & Anti-Untouchability Movements

These movements came from the lower strata of society to challenge the Brahminical hierarchy.

### 1. Satya Shodhak Samaj (Truth Seekers' Society)

* **Founder:** **Jyotiba Phule** (1873) in Maharashtra.
* **Target:** Caste discrimination and Brahmin dominance.
* **Work:** Phule and his wife **Savitribai Phule** opened the first school for girls and untouchables in Pune.
* **Literature:** *Gulamgiri* (Slavery).

### 2. Temple Entry Movement (SNDP)

* **Leader:** **Narayana Guru** (Kerala).
* **Slogan:** *"One Caste, One Religion, One God for Mankind."*
* **Action:** He consecrated a Shiva idol himself (non-Brahmins were forbidden to do so), sparking a silent revolution in Kerala.

### 3. Self-Respect Movement

* **Leader:** **E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker (Periyar)** in Tamil Nadu (1920s).
* **Focus:** Radical anti-Brahminism, burning of Manusmriti, and pride in Dravidian identity.

---

## üìú VI. Legislative Impact (The Results)

The pressure from these reformers forced the British to pass laws:

| Year | Act | Significance |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **1829** | **Abolition of Sati** | Banned the burning of widows (Ram Mohan Roy). |
| **1856** | **Widow Remarriage Act** | Legalized remarriage of widows (Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar). |
| **1872** | **Native Marriage Act** | Banned child marriage and polygamy (limited impact). |
| **1891** | **Age of Consent Act** | Raised the age of consent for girls from 10 to 12 (Opposed by Tilak as "interference"). |
| **1929** | **Sarda Act** | Raised marriage age to 14 for girls and 18 for boys. |

### üöÄ Next Step

This era laid the moral foundation for the political struggle.

---
the **Tribal and Peasant Uprisings** in British India.

---

# üèπ Rebellion from the Roots: Tribal & Peasant Uprisings

*The Struggle for Land and Forest*

> *"The land belongs to the tiller, and the forest belongs to the dweller."*

While the Congress fought for political rights in the cities, the real battle for survival was fought in the forests and fields of rural India. These uprisings were often violent, localized, and directed against the "Unholy Trinity": **The British + The Moneylender + The Zamindar**.

---

## üåæ I. Peasant Movements (Kisan Vidroh)

*The Fight Against High Tax and Oppression*

Peasants revolted when their land was taken away or when taxes became unbearable.

### 1. The Indigo Revolt (Neel Vidroh) - 1859-60

* **Region:** Bengal (Nadia District).
* **The Cause:** European planters forced farmers to grow **Indigo** (for blue dye) instead of rice. The price paid was pitiful, and farmers were beaten if they refused.
* **The Revolt:** Led by **Digambar Biswas** and **Bishnu Biswas**. Farmers collectively refused to grow indigo and attacked planters.
* **Impact:** It was highly organized. The intelligentsia (like Harish Chandra Mukherjee) supported it. The government set up an *Indigo Commission*, which ruled that planters could not use force.
* **Literature:** Captured in the famous play **"Neel Darpan"** by Dinabandhu Mitra.

### 2. The Pabna Agrarian Leagues (1873-85)

* **Region:** East Bengal (Pabna).
* **The Cause:** Zamindars were collecting illegal taxes beyond the legal limit.
* **The Method:** Legal resistance. Peasants formed "Leagues" and fought cases in court against eviction. It was mostly non-violent.

### 3. The Deccan Riots (1875)

* **Region:** Maharashtra (Pune/Ahmednagar).
* **The Cause:** The Ryotwari system coupled with a crash in cotton prices trapped peasants in debt.
* **The Target:** The **Moneylenders** (Marwari/Gujarati Sahukars). Peasants burnt the debt bonds and account books (*Bahi Khatas*).
* **Outcome:** The **Deccan Agriculturists Relief Act (1879)** was passed to protect peasants from arrest for debt.

### 4. Moplah Rebellion (1921)

* **Region:** Malabar (Kerala).
* **The Nature:** Started as a peasant movement against Hindu Zamindars (Jenmis) and the British, but later took a communal turn during the Khilafat Movement.
* **Violence:** It became one of the bloodiest rebellions, leading to martial law.

---

## üèπ II. Tribal Uprisings (Adivasi Vidroh)

*The Fight for the Forest*

Tribals revolted because the British:

1. **Took their land:** Outsiders (*Dikus*) like moneylenders seized tribal land.
2. **Restricted Forest Rights:** New Forest Laws forbade shifting cultivation (*Jhum*) and collecting timber.

### 1. Santhal Hool (1855-56)

* **Region:** Rajmahal Hills (Jharkhand/Bihar).
* **Leaders:** The brothers **Sidhu and Kanhu Murmu**.
* **The Cause:** Moneylenders and police were exploiting the peace-loving Santhals.
* **The Event:** 60,000 Santhals mobilized with bows and arrows. They declared the end of Company rule.
* **Outcome:** Brutally crushed (15,000+ killed). The British created a separate **Santhal Pargana** district to appease them.

### 2. Munda Uprising (Ulgulan) - 1899-1900

* **Region:** Chotanagpur (Ranchi).
* **Leader:** **Birsa Munda** (The "Dharti Aaba" or Father of Earth).
* **The Cause:** The feudal system (*Khuntkatti*) of the Mundas was being destroyed by Jagirdars and missionaries.
* **The Revolt:** Birsa gathered a massive army, attacking police stations and churches.
* **Outcome:** Birsa died in jail (cholera) at age 25. The **Chotanagpur Tenancy Act (1908)** was passed, banning the transfer of tribal land to non-tribals.

### 3. Kol Mutiny (1831)

* **Region:** Chotanagpur.
* **Leader:** Buddho Bhagat.
* **Cause:** Transfer of tribal land to outsider farmers (Sikhs/Muslims) by the British. The Kols burnt over 1,000 villages of the "outsiders."

### 4. Rampa Rebellion (1922-24)

* **Region:** Andhra Pradesh (Godavari Hills).
* **Leader:** **Alluri Sitarama Raju** (Inspired by Gandhi but believed in violence).
* **Cause:** Strict forest laws and exploitation by contractors.
* **Cinema:** This rebellion inspired the recent movie **RRR**.

---

## ‚ö° III. Differences: 1857 vs. Tribal Revolts

| Feature | **Revolt of 1857** | **Tribal Revolts** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Scope** | Regional/North India. | Highly localized and isolated. |
| **Aim** | Restore the old order (Mughals/Peshwas). | Restore tribal rights to forest/land. |
| **Leadership** | Kings, Queens, Sepoys. | Tribal chiefs, Messiah figures (Birsa). |
| **Result** | Changed the Administration (Crown Rule). | Usually resulted in mass slaughter but eventually led to protective laws (Tenancy Acts). |

---

### üìù Summary of Significance

These uprisings proved that the British Empire was never fully accepted by the rural masses. While they were technologically backward (bows vs. guns), their moral resistance paved the way for the later mass movements of the Congress.

---
detailed breakdown of **how Indian Nationalism evolved** and the **linkages** that transformed a subcontinent of scattered kingdoms into a unified nation.

---

# üîó The Evolution & Linkages of Indian Nationalism

> *"India was a nation in the making."* ‚Äî **Surendranath Banerjee**

Nationalism in India did not appear overnight. It was a gradual process where different regions, castes, and classes, which had been separated for centuries, forged **linkages** through a shared history of oppression and a shared vision of the future.

---

## üìà Part 1: The Evolution (Phases of Growth)

The consciousness of "Being Indian" evolved in three distinct stages, widening its base at every step.

### **Phase 1: The Intellectual Awakening (1858‚Äì1905)**

* **The Actors:** The "Bhadralok" (Gentlemen) ‚Äì Lawyers, Doctors, Journalists, Teachers.
* **The Scope:** Urban, elitist, and constitutional.
* **The Nature:** They realized that British rule was economically draining India.
* **The Evolution:** Nationalism was intellectual. It was a debate fought in newspapers and council halls, not on the streets.

### **Phase 2: The Emotional & Cultural Surge (1905‚Äì1918)**

* **The Actors:** The Middle Class, Students, and Women.
* **The Trigger:** The Partition of Bengal (1905).
* **The Nature:** Nationalism became emotional. It used symbols (Ganapati, Bharat Mata), songs (Vande Mataram), and boycotts.
* **The Evolution:** Nationalism moved from "Petition" to "Passive Resistance." It linked politics with culture.

### **Phase 3: The Mass Movement (1919‚Äì1947)**

* **The Actors:** The Peasants, Workers, Tribals, and Capitalists.
* **The Catalyst:** **Mahatma Gandhi**.
* **The Nature:** Gandhi linked the *political* demand for Swaraj with the *social* needs of the poor (Salt, Khadi, Untouchability).
* **The Evolution:** Nationalism became a way of life. The gap between the "Suit-clad Lawyer" and the "Loincloth-wearing Peasant" was bridged.

---

## üîó Part 2: The Linkages of Nationalism

How did a Tamilian in Madras connect with a Punjabi in Lahore? The British inadvertently provided the tools that linked India together.

### **1. Administrative & Political Linkages (The Iron Frame)**

Before the British, India was a patchwork of kingdoms.

* **Uniform Laws:** The British imposed the same laws (*IPC, CrPC*) from the Himalayas to Kanyakumari. A crime in Bengal was judged the same way as in Bombay.
* **Single Authority:** For the first time, one power controlled the entire territory. This created a **"Common Enemy"**‚Äîthe single biggest unifier.

### **2. The Transport Linkage (Railways & Telegraph)**

* **The "Nervous System":** The Railways (1853) were built to move British troops and goods, but they ended up moving ideas.
* **The Mixing:** People of different castes and regions sat in the same railway compartments, breaking social barriers.
* **Speed:** Leaders like Surendranath Banerjee could travel across India to address crowds, turning local grievances into national issues.

### **3. The Linguistic Linkage (English Language)**

India had hundreds of dialects.

* **The Bridge:** English became the *lingua franca* (link language). It allowed the intelligentsia from diverse linguistic regions to communicate.
* **Example:** Dadabhai Naoroji (a Gujarati Parsi) and W.C. Bonnerjee (a Bengali) could run the Congress together because they both spoke English.

### **4. The Economic Linkage (Community of Suffering)**

* **Shared Exploitation:** The British tariff policies hurt the textile weaver in Bengal and the cotton farmer in Maharashtra equally.
* **Drain of Wealth:** The realization that India‚Äôs wealth was being siphoned off to London created a shared economic nationalism. The poverty of India was no longer seen as "fate" but as "policy."

### **5. The Press Linkage (The Spiderweb of News)**

* **The National Library:** Newspapers like *The Hindu*, *Amrita Bazar Patrika*, and *Kesari* acted as a national nervous system.
* **Impact:** A famine in Odisha was reported in Madras newspapers, generating sympathy and solidarity across thousands of miles.

### **6. The Historical Linkage (Rediscovery of Past)**

* **Psychological Unity:** Colonial historians painted Indians as backward. Indian scholars and European Orientalists (like Max Mueller) rediscovered the glory of the Vedas, Ashoka, and the Guptas.
* **Result:** This gave Indians a shared pride. Nationalism needs a "Golden Past" to dream of a "Golden Future."

---

### üí° Summary Diagram: The Web of Nationalism

| **Factor** | **Linkage Created** |
| --- | --- |
| **Railways** | Physical Linkage (Geography) |
| **English** | Intellectual Linkage (Communication) |
| **British Laws** | Administrative Linkage (Uniformity) |
| **Poverty** | Emotional Linkage (Shared Suffering) |
| **Press** | Information Linkage (Awareness) |

### üöÄ Next Step

The stage is now fully unified. The "Nation" is ready, but it needs a leader to direct this energy.


---
 **Revolutionary Terrorism Phase II (1920s‚Äì1930s)**, often called the "Socialist Phase" of the revolutionary struggle.

---

# üí£ Phase II: The Socialist Turn (1922‚Äì1934)

*From "Bande Mataram" to "Inquilab Zindabad"*

> *"The bomb was necessary to awaken England from her dreams... We dropped the bomb on the floor of the Assembly Chamber to make the deaf hear."* ‚Äî **Bhagat Singh**

The second wave of revolutionary activity rose from the ashes of the Non-Cooperation Movement (1922). When Mahatma Gandhi suddenly withdrew the movement after the **Chauri Chaura** incident, the youth felt betrayed. Disillusioned with non-violence, they returned to arms‚Äîbut this time, with a new ideology: **Socialism**.

---

## üö© 1. North India: The Hindustan Republican Association (HRA)

The revolutionaries in Punjab, UP, and Bihar united to form a pan-Indian organization.

### **A. Formation & The Kakori Train Action**

* **Founded:** 1924 in Kanpur by **Ramprasad Bismil**, **Sachin Sanyal**, and **Jogesh Chandra Chatterjee**.
* **Goal:** To establish a "Federal Republic of United States of India" via armed revolution.
* **The Kakori Train Action (Aug 9, 1925):**
* **The Plan:** To rob the government treasury bag from the 8-Down train at Kakori (near Lucknow) to buy arms.
* **The Execution:** Led by Ramprasad Bismil and Ashfaqullah Khan. They successfully looted the train but left a shawl behind, leading to their arrest.
* **The Consequence:**
* **Hanged:** Ramprasad Bismil, Ashfaqullah Khan, Roshan Singh, Rajendra Lahiri.
* **Famous Line:** Bismil wrote *"Sarfaroshi ki tamanna ab hamare dil mein hai"* (The desire for sacrifice is now in our hearts).





### **B. Rebirth: HSRA (The Socialist Shift)**

* **The Change:** Under the leadership of **Chandrashekhar Azad** and **Bhagat Singh**, the HRA was reorganized in 1928 at Feroz Shah Kotla (Delhi).
* **New Name:** **Hindustan Socialist Republican Association (HSRA)**.
* **New Ideology:** It wasn't just about killing Britishers; it was about ending exploitation by capitalists and landlords (Marxist influence).

### **C. Saunders' Murder (Lahore Conspiracy)**

* **The Trigger:** **Lala Lajpat Rai** died after being brutally lathi-charged by the police (led by James Scott) during the Anti-Simon Commission protests (1928).
* **The Revenge:** Bhagat Singh, Rajguru, and Sukhdev planned to kill Scott. Mistakenly, they killed the ASP, **John Saunders**.
* **The Escape:** They escaped Lahore; Bhagat Singh cut his hair and shaved his beard to evade capture.

### **D. Central Assembly Bombing (1929)**

* **The Logic:** The government was passing two repressive bills: the *Public Safety Bill* and the *Trade Disputes Bill*.
* **The Act:** **Bhagat Singh** and **Batukeshwar Dutt** threw harmless smoke bombs into the Central Legislative Assembly (Delhi) to protest. They threw leaflets and shouted **"Inquilab Zindabad!"** (Long Live Revolution).
* **The Arrest:** They stood there and surrendered voluntarily to use the court as a platform to spread their ideology.

### **E. Martyrdom**

* Bhagat Singh, Sukhdev, and Rajguru were tried in the Lahore Conspiracy Case and hanged on **March 23, 1931**.
* **Chandrashekhar Azad** died fighting the police at **Alfred Park (Allahabad)** in Feb 1931. He shot himself with the last bullet to remain "Azad" (Free).

---

## üå¥ 2. Bengal: The Chittagong Armoury Raid

While North India turned Socialist, Bengal remained the hub of highly organized guerilla warfare.

### **A. The Masterda: Surya Sen**

* **Leader:** **Surya Sen**, a humble school teacher ("Masterda").
* **Ideology:** Unlike the individual heroism of the past, he believed in organized armed uprising (inspired by the Irish Easter Rising).
* **Organization:** Indian Republican Army (Chittagong Branch).

### **B. The Raid (April 18, 1930)**

* **The Plan:** Seize the two armouries (Police and Auxiliary Force) in Chittagong, cut telegraph/telephone lines, and disrupt train movements to isolate Chittagong from the rest of India.
* **The Action:** 65 revolutionaries raided the armouries. They captured the arms but failed to find ammunition. They hoisted the National Flag and declared a Provisional Revolutionary Government.
* **Jalalabad Hill Battle:** The group retreated to the Jalalabad Hills where they fought a heroic battle against British machine guns. 12 revolutionaries died.
* **The End:** Surya Sen was eventually captured (betrayed by a local), brutally tortured, and hanged in 1934.

---

## üë© 3. Women in Revolution

Phase II saw unprecedented participation of women, who moved from being "messengers" to "shooters."

* **Pritilata Waddedar:** Led a raid on the European Club in Chittagong (which had a sign "Dogs and Indians not allowed"). She consumed cyanide to avoid arrest.
* **Kalpana Datta:** A close associate of Surya Sen; arrested and sentenced to life imprisonment.
* **Bina Das:** Fired shots at the Governor of Bengal (Stanley Jackson) inside the Convocation Hall of Calcutta University while receiving her degree.
* **Shanti Ghosh & Suniti Chandheri:** Two schoolgirls who shot dead the District Magistrate of Comilla.

---

## üß† 4. Ideological Evolution: What changed?

| Feature | **Phase I (1907‚Äì1917)** | **Phase II (1922‚Äì1934)** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Ideology** | Hindu Revivalism (Kali, Shivaji). | **Socialism / Marxism / Secularism**. |
| **Goal** | Drive out the British. | Drive out British + End Class Exploitation. |
| **Method** | Individual Assassinations. | Organized Raids / Open Battles. |
| **Religion** | Heavy use of religious oaths. | Atheism (Bhagat Singh wrote *"Why I am an Atheist"*). |

### üöÄ Next Step

The revolutionary flame dimmed by the mid-1930s as many leaders joined the Communist Party or the Congress Socialist Party.

---
---

# üìú Part 1: Morley-Minto Reforms (Indian Councils Act, 1909)

*The Poisoned Chalice*

> *"We are sowing dragon's teeth, and the harvest will be bitter."* ‚Äî **Lord Morley** (Secretary of State) writing to Lord Minto (Viceroy).

Following the chaos of the **Swadeshi Movement**, the British adopted a **"Carrot and Stick"** policy.

* **The Stick:** Crush the Extremists (Tilak was jailed).
* **The Carrot:** Conciliate the Moderates and Muslims with constitutional reforms.

### 1. Key Provisions

* **Expansion of Councils:** The size of the Legislative Councils was increased.
* *Central Council:* From 16 to 60 members.
* *Provincial Councils:* Doubled (e.g., Bengal, Madras, Bombay).


* **First Indian in Executive Council:** For the first time, an Indian was admitted to the Viceroy's powerful **Executive Council** (the real government).
* **Satyendra Prasanna (S.P.) Sinha** was appointed as the Law Member.


* **Increased Powers:** Members could now discuss the **Budget** and move resolutions (though they couldn't vote on it). They could ask "Supplementary Questions."

### 2. The Controversial Feature: Separate Electorates

This was the most damaging part of the act.

* **The Concept:** Seats were reserved for Muslims where **only Muslims could vote for Muslim candidates**.
* **The Logic:** It treated Muslims as a separate political entity, distinct from the rest of the nation.
* **The Result:** It incentivized Muslim leaders to appeal only to their religion, not to the broader nation, to get elected.

### 3. Critical Assessment

While it looked like a reform, it was a shadow.

* **No Responsibility:** The councils were still "advisory." The Viceroy retained veto power.
* **Shadow Democracy:** Only a tiny elite (landlords, rich traders) could vote.
* **Communal Rift:** It officially recognized the "Two-Nation" theory in embryo.

---

# ‚ò™Ô∏è Part 2: The Growth of Communalism

*The Architecture of Division*

Communalism in India wasn't an overnight phenomenon; it was carefully cultivated over decades.

### 1. The British Policy of "Divide and Rule"

* **Pre-1857:** The British feared the Muslims (former rulers) and suppressed them.
* **Post-1858:** After seeing Hindu-Muslim unity in the 1857 Revolt, they decided to split them.
* **Post-1870:** They began favoring Muslims to counter the rising "Hindu" nationalism of the Congress. W.W. Hunter‚Äôs book *The Indian Musalmans* urged the government to ally with Muslims.

### 2. Formation of the Muslim League (1906)

* **The Shimla Deputation:** A group of elite Muslims led by **Aga Khan** met Viceroy Minto in Shimla. They demanded separate electorates, arguing that Muslims were not a minority but a "political power."
* **The Founding:** In December 1906, at Dhaka, the **All India Muslim League** was founded by **Nawab Salimullah** of Dhaka.
* **Goal:** To support the British Government and protect Muslim political rights (specifically against the "Hindu" Congress).

### 3. Factors Fueling Communalism

* **Religious Revivalism:**
* *Hindu:* The Arya Samaj‚Äôs **Shuddhi** (re-conversion) and Cow Protection movements alarmed Muslims.
* *Muslim:* The Wahabi movement and Tabligh movement emphasized a distinct Islamic identity.


* **Communal History:** British historians (like James Mill) divided Indian history into "Hindu Period" and "Muslim Period," painting the medieval era as a time of Hindu oppression by Muslim tyrants.
* **Economic Competition:** Middle-class Muslims struggled to compete with the earlier-educated Hindus for government jobs, leading to resentment (e.g., the Hindi-Urdu controversy).

### 4. Evolution Timeline (The Vicious Cycle)

1. **1909:** Separate Electorates (Legalized communalism).
2. **1916:** **Lucknow Pact** (Congress accepted Separate Electorates‚Äîa strategic blunder).
3. **1920s:** Post-Non-Cooperation, communal riots broke out. The Hindu Mahasabha and RSS (1925) rose on one side; the League radicalized on the other.
4. **1937:** Congress won elections; the League felt alienated. Jinnah declared "Islam is in Danger."
5. **1940:** **Lahore Resolution** (Pakistan Resolution). The demand for a separate nation became official.

### üöÄ Next Step

The communal wedge has been driven.


---
the **Gandhian Era (Part I: 1915‚Äì1919)**, covering his arrival and the early "laboratory experiments" of Satyagraha.

---

# üßò The Arrival of the Mahatma (1915)

> *"I am not a visionary. I claim to be a practical idealist."* ‚Äî **M.K. Gandhi**

Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi returned to India from South Africa on **January 9, 1915** (celebrated today as *Pravasi Bharatiya Divas*). He was already a legend for his struggle against racial laws in South Africa, but he was a stranger to Indian politics.

### **The "Silent" Year**

His political guru, **Gopal Krishna Gokhale**, gave him advice that shaped history: *"Keep your ears open, but your mouth shut for one year."*

* Gandhi spent 1915‚Äì1916 touring the villages of India in third-class railway compartments to understand the true condition of the masses.
* He founded the **Sabarmati Ashram** in Ahmedabad (1916) to train workers in Satyagraha.

---

# üöú I. The Three Early Experiments (1917‚Äì1918)

Before launching a national war, Gandhi tested his weapons‚Äî**Satyagraha** (Truth-force) and **Ahimsa** (Non-violence)‚Äîin three localized battles.

### 1. Champaran Satyagraha (1917) ‚Äì *First Civil Disobedience*

* **The Place:** Bihar.
* **The Issue:** The **Tinkathia System**. European planters forced peasants to grow **Indigo** on 3/20th of their land. Since German synthetic dyes had ruined the market, planters demanded illegal dues (*Sharahbeshi*) to release peasants from this obligation.
* **The Event:**
* Gandhi was invited by a local peasant, **Raj Kumar Shukla**.
* Upon arrival, the Commissioner ordered Gandhi to leave the district. Gandhi **defied the order** and pleaded guilty, saying he was obeying "the higher law of our being‚Äîthe voice of conscience."
* The government, stunned, withdrew the case and allowed him to investigate.


* **The Outcome:** A committee was formed (with Gandhi as a member). The Tinkathia system was abolished, and planters refunded 25% of the illegal money.
* **Significance:** It was the first victory of Civil Disobedience in India.

### 2. Ahmedabad Mill Strike (1918) ‚Äì *First Hunger Strike*

* **The Place:** Gujarat.
* **The Issue:** A dispute between cotton mill owners and workers over the discontinuation of the **"Plague Bonus."**
* Workers demanded a **50%** hike (due to WWI inflation).
* Owners offered only **20%**.


* **The Event:** Gandhi intervened. He asked workers to strike but remain non-violent. When morale dipped, Gandhi undertook a **Fast unto Death** to strengthen their resolve.
* **The Outcome:** The owners panicked (fearing bad publicity) and agreed to arbitration. The workers got a **35%** wage hike.

### 3. Kheda Satyagraha (1918) ‚Äì *First Non-Cooperation*

* **The Place:** Gujarat.
* **The Issue:** Crops had failed due to drought. According to the **Revenue Code**, if the yield was less than 1/4th of normal, the land tax should be remitted. The British government refused and demanded full tax.
* **The Event:** Gandhi (supported by **Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel** and Indulal Yagnik) asked peasants to **refuse to pay taxes** even if their land was confiscated.
* **The Outcome:** The government secretly issued instructions to collect tax only from those who could afford to pay.
* **Significance:** It awakened the peasantry of Gujarat, who became Gandhi's loyal base.

---

# ü¶Ö II. The Turning Point: Rowlatt Act & Jallianwala Bagh (1919)

The localized leader became a national icon when the British passed the "Black Act."

### **1. The Rowlatt Act (March 1919)**

* **Official Name:** Anarchical and Revolutionary Crimes Act.
* **The Law:** It allowed the government to imprison any person without trial for 2 years.
* **Popular Slogan:** *"Na Dalil, Na Vakil, Na Appeal"* (No argument, no lawyer, no appeal).
* **Gandhi's Response:** He organized the **Rowlatt Satyagraha**‚Äîthe first all-India mass strike (*Hartal*) on April 6, 1919.

### **2. Jallianwala Bagh Massacre (April 13, 1919)**

* **The Context:** Punjab was boiling. Two leaders, **Dr. Saifuddin Kitchlew** and **Dr. Satyapal**, were arrested.
* **The Event:** On Baisakhi day, a large unarmed crowd gathered in Jallianwala Bagh (Amritsar) to protest peacefully.
* **The Butcher:** **General Dyer** blocked the only exit and ordered his troops to fire. They fired 1,650 rounds for 10 minutes.
* **The Toll:** Official estimates said 379 dead; reality was over 1,000.
* **The Aftermath:**
* **Rabindranath Tagore** renounced his Knighthood.
* Gandhi was horrified. He called off the Rowlatt Satyagraha, calling it a **"Himalayan Blunder"** because the masses were not yet ready for non-violence.



### üìù Summary Table of Early Movements

| Year | Movement | Nature of Struggle | Result |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **1917** | **Champaran** | First Civil Disobedience | Indigo system abolished. |
| **1918** | **Ahmedabad** | First Hunger Strike | 35% wage hike secured. |
| **1918** | **Kheda** | First Non-Cooperation | Tax collection relaxed. |
| **1919** | **Rowlatt** | First Mass Strike | Turned violent (Jallianwala Bagh); withdrawn. |

### üöÄ Next Step

The brutality of Jallianwala Bagh and the betrayal of the Khilafat issue set the stage for the first "Grand" movement.



---
 **Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms (1919)** and the subsequent ideological split within the Congress between the **Swarajists and No-Changers**.

---

# üìú Part 1: Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms (1919)

*The Experiment of "Dyarchy"*

> *"The reforms were unworthy of England to offer and India to accept."* ‚Äî **Annie Besant**

In 1917, amidst World War I, **Edwin Montagu** (Secretary of State for India) made a historic declaration: the British goal was the *"progressive realization of **responsible government** in India."* This led to the **Government of India Act, 1919**.

### 1. Key Features: The System of "Dyarchy"

The Act introduced a dual system of governance in the **Provinces** called **Dyarchy** (Rule of Two).

* **Reserved Subjects:** Key areas like **Law & Order, Finance, Land Revenue,** and **Irrigation** were kept under the **Governor** and his Executive Council (bureaucrats). They were *not* responsible to the legislature.
* **Transferred Subjects:** "Nation-building" departments like **Education, Health, Agriculture,** and **Local Self-Government** were given to **Indian Ministers** elected by the people. They *were* responsible to the legislature.
* *The Trap:* Ministers had responsibilities but no money (Finance was "Reserved"). If schools failed, the Indian minister was blamed, even if the British Governor refused to release funds.



### 2. Changes at the Center

* **Bicameralism:** For the first time, a two-house legislature was introduced at the Center:
1. **Council of State (Upper House):** 60 members (elected by the super-rich).
2. **Central Legislative Assembly (Lower House):** 145 members.


* **Direct Elections:** Introduced for the first time, though the franchise was extremely limited (only ~10% of adult males could vote based on high property/tax criteria).

### 3. Significance

* It separated **Provincial Budgets** from the Central Budget.
* It established a **Public Service Commission** for recruiting civil servants.
* It extended **Separate Electorates** to Sikhs, Christians, Anglo-Indians, and Europeans (widening the communal divide).

---

# üèõÔ∏è Part 2: Swarajists vs. No-Changers (1922‚Äì1925)

*To Enter or To Boycott?*

After Gandhi withdrew the **Non-Cooperation Movement** (following the Chauri Chaura incident in 1922) and was arrested, a vacuum emerged. The Congress split into two camps on the future strategy.

### 1. The Pro-Changers (The Swarajists)

* **Leaders:** **C.R. Das** (Deshbandhu) and **Motilal Nehru**.
* **Philosophy:** **"Council Entry."** They argued that boycotting the elections (a tactic of 1920) was no longer working.
* **Strategy:** They wanted to enter the Legislative Councils not to work *with* the British, but to **"wreck them from within."**
* Obstruct government proceedings.
* Vote down the budget.
* Expose the "sham" of the 1919 Act to the world.


* **Slogan:** *"To End it or Mend it."*

### 2. The No-Changers (The Orthodox Gandhians)

* **Leaders:** **Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel**, **Dr. Rajendra Prasad**, **C. Rajagopalachari**, **M.A. Ansari**.
* **Philosophy:** They opposed Council Entry, fearing it would lead to corruption and a loss of revolutionary zeal ("parliamentary politics corrupts").
* **Strategy:** Continue the boycott and focus entirely on **Constructive Work** in the villages until Gandhi returned:
* Promotion of **Khadi** (Spinning).
* **Hindu-Muslim Unity**.
* Removal of **Untouchability**.



### 3. The Formation of the Swaraj Party (1923)

At the **Gaya Session (1922)**, the No-Changers defeated the proposal for Council Entry.

* **The Split:** C.R. Das resigned as Congress President and formed the **Congress-Khilafat Swaraj Party** (Swaraj Party) on **January 1, 1923**.
* **The Truce:** Unlike the 1907 Surat Split, both sides were wise enough to avoid a permanent break. In 1923, a compromise allowed the Swarajists to contest elections as a "Group within the Congress," while No-Changers did rural work.

### 4. Achievements of the Swarajists

In the **1923 Elections**, they won 42 out of 101 elected seats in the Central Assembly.

* **Vithalbhai Patel** became the **first Indian Speaker** of the Central Legislative Assembly (1925)‚Äîa massive prestige victory.
* They successfully stalled the budget and forced the Viceroy to use his unpopular "Veto" power repeatedly, exposing the lack of democracy.
* They blocked the **Public Safety Bill** (1928), which was aimed at crushing communists/socialists.

### 5. Decline

After the death of **C.R. Das** in 1925, the party weakened. By 1929, realizing that obstruction alone wouldn't bring freedom, they merged back into the mainstream Congress for the **Civil Disobedience Movement**.



---



the **Non-Cooperation Movement (1920‚Äì1922)** and the **Khilafat Movement**, the first time India stood up as one to say "No" to the British Empire.

---

# ü§ù The Great Unification: Khilafat & Non-Cooperation (1920‚Äì1922)

*The Era of Mass Struggle*

> *"This Satanic government cannot be mended, it must be ended."* ‚Äî **Mahatma Gandhi**

By 1920, the British had broken every promise made during WWI. The Rowlatt Act, the Jallianwala Bagh massacre, and the betrayal of the Turkish Sultan forced Gandhi to launch the first mass movement.

---

## ‚ò™Ô∏è 1. The Khilafat Issue (The Catalyst)

* **The Cause:** In World War I, Turkey (Ottoman Empire) fought against Britain and lost. The British decided to dismember Turkey and remove the **Sultan**, who was regarded as the **Khalifa** (Religious Head) of Muslims worldwide.
* **The Anger:** Indian Muslims were furious. They formed the **Khilafat Committee** led by the **Ali Brothers** (Shaukat Ali and Mohammad Ali), Maulana Azad, and Hasrat Mohani.
* **Gandhi‚Äôs Masterstroke:** Gandhi saw this as *"an opportunity for uniting Hindus and Muslims that would not arise in a hundred years."* He supported the Khilafat cause to bring Muslims into the nationalist fold.

---

## üö´ 2. The Non-Cooperation Movement (NCM)

### **A. The Nagpur Session (Dec 1920)**

The Indian National Congress endorsed the movement. Crucially, the goal of the Congress changed from "Constitutional agitation" to **"Swaraj by peaceful and legitimate means."**

### **B. The Program (Negative & Positive)**

| **Negative Program (Boycott)** | **Positive Program (Construction)** |
| --- | --- |
| **Boycott of Titles:** Gandhi returned his *Kaiser-i-Hind* medal; Tagore returned his Knighthood. | **National Schools:** Students left government schools. Jamia Millia Islamia, Bihar Vidyapith, and Kashi Vidyapith were founded. |
| **Boycott of Courts:** Lawyers like C.R. Das, Motilal Nehru, and Sardar Patel gave up lucrative practices. | **Panchayats:** Villagers established private arbitration courts to settle disputes. |
| **Boycott of Foreign Cloth:** Massive bonfires of foreign clothes. Imports dropped by half. | **Khadi & Spinning:** The **Charkha** became the symbol of freedom. Khadi was the "livery of freedom." |
| **Boycott of Elections:** Congress refused to participate in the 1920 elections. | **Hindu-Muslim Unity** and removal of **Untouchability**. |

---

## üåä 3. The Spread of the Movement

The movement unleashed energy that surprised even the leaders.

* **Students:** Thousands left colleges to join the protests. **Subhash Chandra Bose** resigned from the Civil Service (ICS) to join.
* **Peasants:**
* In **Awadh**, peasants led by Baba Ramchandra refused to pay illegal taxes.
* In **Andhra**, Alluri Sitarama Raju led tribals in the Rampa Rebellion.


* **The Prince of Wales Visit (1921):** When the Prince visited India, he was greeted by empty streets and closed shops (*Hartals*) everywhere.

---

## üî• 4. The Withdrawal: Chauri Chaura Incident

By late 1921, the movement was at its peak. The British were nervous; 30,000 people were in jail. Gandhi was planning the next phase (Civil Disobedience) in Bardoli.

### **The Incident (Feb 5, 1922)**

* **Location:** **Chauri Chaura**, a small village in Gorakhpur district (UP).
* **The Event:** Police fired on a peaceful procession. The angry mob chased the policemen into the station and **set it on fire**.
* **The Toll:** **22 policemen** were burnt alive.

### **Gandhi‚Äôs Reaction (Feb 12, 1922)**

Gandhi was shaken. He believed that a violent mob could not lead a non-violent nation. Despite opposition from Nehru and Subhash Bose (who called it a "National Calamity"), Gandhi **called off** the movement unilaterally via the **Bardoli Resolution**.

> *"I would rather work for God alone than for a mob that is violent."*

---

## üìâ 5. Significance & Impact

Though it ended abruptly, the NCM transformed India forever.

1. **Fear Gone:** The fear of the British police and prison vanished from the minds of the common people. Going to jail became a badge of honor.
2. **Mass Reach:** The Congress became a true mass party. It reached villages, and the membership fee was reduced to **4 Annas** to allow the poor to join.
3. **Khadi:** The white Gandhi cap and Khadi kurta became the uniform of the nationalist.

### **The Aftermath**

* **Gandhi Arrested (March 1922):** The British took advantage of the withdrawal and arrested Gandhi. He was sentenced to **6 years** in prison for sedition (famously pleading guilty).
* **The Split:** The Congress split into two factions regarding the future course:
* **Pro-Changers (Swarajists):** C.R. Das & Motilal Nehru wanted to enter the Legislative Councils to "wreck them from within."
* **No-Changers:** Sardar Patel & Rajendra Prasad wanted to continue Gandhi‚Äôs constructive rural work.


---

period of **Political Void & Resurgence (1923‚Äì1928)**, marked by the parliamentary battles of the Swarajists and the violent heroism of the revolutionaries.

---

# üèõÔ∏è Part 1: The Swaraj Party (1923‚Äì1928)

*Wrecking from Within*

> *"To mend it or end it."* ‚Äî **C.R. Das**

After Gandhi withdrew the Non-Cooperation Movement (1922) and was arrested, a deep depression filled the political atmosphere. The Congress split into two camps on how to proceed.

### 1. The Great Debate: Pro-Changers vs. No-Changers

* **Pro-Changers (The Swarajists):** Led by **C.R. Das** (Deshbandhu) and **Motilal Nehru**.
* *Strategy:* **"Council Entry."** They argued that boycotting elections was useless. Instead, they should enter the Legislative Councils, expose their hollowness, and obstruct British work ("End or Mend").


* **No-Changers (The Gandhians):** Led by **Sardar Patel**, **Rajendra Prasad**, and **C. Rajagopalachari**.
* *Strategy:* Continue the boycott. Focus on **Constructive Work** (Khadi, Hindu-Muslim unity, anti-untouchability) in villages until Gandhi returned.



### 2. Formation of the Swaraj Party (Jan 1, 1923)

At the Gaya Session (1922), the Congress rejected the "Council Entry" proposal. C.R. Das resigned as President and formed the **Congress-Khilafat Swaraj Party** (Swaraj Party) within the Congress.

### 3. Achievements of the Swarajists

In the 1923 elections, they won 42 out of 101 seats in the Central Legislative Assembly.

* **Vithalbhai Patel** became the **first Indian Speaker** of the Central Assembly (1925)‚Äîa massive prestige victory.
* They successfully stalled the budget and embarrassed the government repeatedly.
* They exposed the **"Public Safety Bill"** (intended to curb communists) as a tool of oppression.

### 4. The Decline

The party weakened after the death of **C.R. Das** in 1925. By 1926, communal elements entered the party, and it slowly merged back into the mainstream Congress agitation.

---

# üí£ Part 2: Revolutionary Phase II (1924‚Äì1929)

*The Socialist Turn*

With Gandhi in jail and the Swarajists busy in debates, the youth felt leaderless. The "Old Guard" revolutionaries regrouped, this time influenced by the **Russian Revolution (1917)** and **Socialism**.

### 1. The Hindustan Republican Association (HRA) - 1924

* **Founders:** Ramprasad Bismil, Sachin Sanyal, Jogesh Chandra Chatterjee (in Kanpur).
* **Goal:** Armed revolution to establish a "Federal Republic of United States of India."
* **Major Event: The Kakori Train Action (Aug 9, 1925)**
* *Objective:* Steal government money to buy weapons.
* *Action:* Revolutionaries stopped the 8-Down train at Kakori (near Lucknow) and looted the treasury.
* *Outcome:* The British launched a massive manhunt.
* **Hanged:** **Ramprasad Bismil** (*"Sarfaroshi ki tamanna..."*), **Ashfaqullah Khan**, **Roshan Singh**, **Rajendra Lahiri**.
* **Imprisoned:** Sachin Sanyal (Cellular Jail).





### 2. The Hindustan Socialist Republican Association (HSRA) - 1928

* **Reorganization:** The survivors, led by **Chandrashekhar Azad**, met at Feroz Shah Kotla (Delhi) in 1928. They added the word **"Socialist"** to their name, thanks to **Bhagat Singh**.
* **New Goal:** Not just freedom from British, but freedom from poverty and class exploitation.

### 3. Key Actions of HSRA

* **Saunders' Murder (Lahore Conspiracy, Dec 1928):**
* *Context:* **Lala Lajpat Rai** died after a brutal lathi charge by James Scott during the Anti-Simon Commission protests.
* *Revenge:* Bhagat Singh, Azad, and Rajguru planned to kill Scott but mistakenly killed the ASP, **John Saunders**.


* **Central Assembly Bombing (April 8, 1929):**
* *Motive:* To protest the repressive **Public Safety Bill** and **Trade Disputes Bill**.
* *Action:* **Bhagat Singh** and **Batukeshwar Dutt** threw harmless smoke bombs into the Assembly. They didn't run away; they stood and shouted **"Inquilab Zindabad!"**
* *Reason:* *"To make the deaf hear"* and use the court trial as a platform to spread their ideology to the masses.



### 4. The End of the Heroes

* **Jatin Das:** Died in Lahore Jail after a **63-day hunger strike** demanding better treatment for political prisoners.
* **Martyrdom:** Bhagat Singh, Sukhdev, and Rajguru were hanged on **March 23, 1931**.
* **Chandrashekhar Azad:** Shot himself during a police encounter at **Alfred Park, Allahabad** (Feb 1931), keeping his vow never to be captured alive.

---

### üìù Summary of the Era

This period was the "bridge" between the two great Gandhian movements.

1. **Political:** The Swarajists kept the spirit of resistance alive in the legislature.
2. **Militant:** The Revolutionaries inspired a generation with their supreme sacrifice and socialist ideas.

---
detailed breakdown of the **Simon Commission (1927)** and the **Nehru Report (1928)**, the two events that reignited the Indian freedom struggle and united the nation against a common insult.

---

# ‚ö™ Part 1: The Simon Commission (1927)

*The All-White Insult*

> *"Go Back Simon!"* ‚Äî **Yusuf Meherally** (Popularized by Lala Lajpat Rai)

### 1. Why was it appointed?

The **Government of India Act 1919** (Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms) had a provision that a commission would be appointed after **10 years** to review the working of the act and suggest further constitutional reforms.

* **Premature Arrival:** The British Conservative government, fearing defeat by the Labour Party in upcoming elections, sent the commission **two years early** (in 1927) to ensure they controlled India's future.

### 2. The Composition (The Insult)

* **Chairman:** **Sir John Simon**.
* **Members:** **7 Members** (All British MPs, including Clement Attlee, future PM).
* **The Problem:** There was **not a single Indian member**. The British government effectively told India: *"You are incapable of deciding your own constitution; we will decide it for you."*

### 3. The Reaction: Complete Boycott

This racial arrogance united all Indian political parties.

* **The Congress:** Decided to boycott the commission at every stage and in every form.
* **The Muslim League:** Even the Jinnah faction of the League joined the boycott (though the Shafi faction supported it).
* **The Hindu Mahasabha & Liberals:** Also joined the protest.

### 4. The Protests

* **Arrival (Feb 3, 1928):** When the commission landed in Bombay, it was greeted with a country-wide **Hartal** (strike) and black flags.
* **Lahore (Oct 30, 1928):** **Lala Lajpat Rai** led a peaceful procession. The police superintendent, **James Scott**, ordered a brutal lathi charge.
* Lajpat Rai was struck on the chest and died a few weeks later.
* *His Dying Words:* *"Every blow aimed at me is a nail in the coffin of British Imperialism."*
* *(Consequence: Bhagat Singh killed Saunders to avenge this).*



---

# üìú Part 2: The Nehru Report (1928)

*India's First Constitution Draft*

> *"If you are so capable, why don't you draft your own constitution that all parties agree upon?"* ‚Äî **Lord Birkenhead** (Secretary of State)
