Lord Birkenhead mocked the Indian leaders, claiming they were too divided to agree on anything. The Congress accepted the challenge.

### 1. The All Parties Conference

* **Date:** February & May 1928.
* **Chairman:** **Motilal Nehru** (Father of Jawaharlal Nehru).
* **Secretary:** **Jawaharlal Nehru**.
* **Task:** To draft a constitution for India.

### 2. Key Recommendations of the Report

It was a visionary document that laid the foundation for the future Constitution of India (1950).

* **Dominion Status:** India would be a self-governing dominion within the British Empire (like Canada/Australia). *This was the most controversial point.*
* **Rejection of Separate Electorates:** It proposed **Joint Electorates** with reservation of seats for Muslims only where they were a minority.
* **Fundamental Rights:** Demanded 19 rights, including equal rights for women and the right to form unions.
* **Linguistic Provinces:** Suggested reorganizing states based on language.
* **Secularism:** Complete separation of State and Religion.

### 3. The Reaction: The Consensus Breaks

While the report was brilliant, it failed to satisfy everyone.

* **Muslim League (Jinnah):** Jinnah rejected the report because it removed Separate Electorates. He proposed his famous **"14 Points"** (demanding 1/3rd seats in Central Assembly, weak center, and residual powers to provinces). The deadlock between Nehru Report and Jinnah's 14 Points widened the Hindu-Muslim gap.
* **Young Leaders (Jawaharlal Nehru & Subhash Bose):** They were angry with the demand for "Dominion Status." They wanted **"Purna Swaraj"** (Complete Independence).

---

# ‚è≥ Part 3: The Ultimatum (Calcutta Session, 1928)

To resolve the conflict between the "Old Guard" (Motilal/Gandhi who wanted Dominion Status) and the "Young Turks" (Nehru/Bose who wanted Independence), a compromise was reached at the Calcutta Session.

* **The Ultimatum:** The Congress told the British: *"Accept the Nehru Report (Dominion Status) by **December 31, 1929**. If you do not, we will demand **Purna Swaraj** and launch a mass Civil Disobedience Movement."*

The British government ignored the ultimatum. The clock ticked towards midnight of 1929.

### üöÄ Next Step

The deadline has passed. The stage is set for the most historic session in Congress history.


---
Detailed breakdown of the historic **Lahore Session (1929)** and the **Purna Swaraj Declaration**, the moment India decided to settle for nothing less than total freedom.

---

# üáÆüá≥ The Lahore Session (1929)

*The Declaration of Independence*

> *"We believe that it is the inalienable right of the Indian people, as of any other people, to have freedom and to enjoy the fruits of their toil."* ‚Äî **Purna Swaraj Pledge**

### 1. The Context (The Ultimatum Expires)

At the Calcutta Session (1928), the Congress gave the British a one-year ultimatum: accept the **Nehru Report** (Dominion Status) by **December 31, 1929**, or face a demand for complete independence.
The British government (under Viceroy Lord Irwin) remained silent and arrogant. The time for compromise was over.

### 2. The Presidency (Passing the Torch)

* **The President:** **Jawaharlal Nehru**.
* **Significance:** Gandhi refused the presidency and nominated Nehru. This symbolized the transfer of leadership from the "Old Guard" to the **"Young Blood"**. Nehru, a socialist and republican, represented the modern, youthful face of India.

### 3. The Historic Resolution (Purna Swaraj)

On **December 19, 1929**, the Congress passed the historic resolution:

* **Goal:** The word *Swaraj* in the Congress constitution would henceforth mean **"Complete Independence"** (total severance from the British connection), not just Dominion Status.
* **Boycott:** Round Table Conferences would be boycotted.
* **Action:** The Congress Working Committee was authorized to launch a **Civil Disobedience Movement** (including non-payment of taxes).

### 4. Midnight on River Ravi (Dec 31, 1929)

As the clock struck midnight, bringing in the New Year of 1930:

* Jawaharlal Nehru hoisted the newly adopted **Tricolour Flag** of Indian independence on the banks of the **River Ravi** in Lahore.
* Cries of *"Inquilab Zindabad"* (Long Live Revolution) echoed through the cold night.

---

# üìú The Independence Pledge (January 26, 1930)

The Congress decided to observe **January 26, 1930**, as the first **"Independence Day"** (Purna Swaraj Day). Public meetings were held all over the country where people took a pledge.

### **Key Points of the Pledge:**

1. **Right to Freedom:** Freedom is the inalienable right of Indians.
2. **Economic Ruin:** The British have ruined India economically, politically, culturally, and spiritually.
3. **Crime against Man & God:** To submit to such a rule is a "crime against man and God."
4. **Action:** We will prepare for Civil Disobedience, including non-payment of taxes.

### **Why January 26?**

This date became sacred in Indian history.

* When India finally became independent on August 15, 1947, the leaders wanted to remember the original "Independence Day."
* Therefore, the **Constitution of India** was formally adopted on **January 26, 1950**, making it **Republic Day**.

---

### üöÄ Next Step

The declaration has been made. Now, words must be turned into action. Gandhi needs a symbol to launch the Civil Disobedience Movement. He finds it in a pinch of salt.


---

a detailed breakdown of the **Civil Disobedience Movement (1930)** and the historic **Dandi March**, where a pinch of salt shook the mighty British Empire.

---

# üßÇ Civil Disobedience Movement (1930‚Äì1934)

*The Battle of Right against Might*

> *"I want world sympathy in this battle of Right against Might."* ‚Äî **Mahatma Gandhi (at Dandi)**

After the Purna Swaraj declaration, Gandhi looked for a symbol that would unite every Indian‚ÄîHindu or Muslim, rich or poor. He found it in **Salt**.

### 1. Why Salt?

* **Universal Need:** Everyone needs salt. It is a basic necessity of life.
* **The Injustice:** The British government had a monopoly on salt production and levied a heavy tax on it. Even the poorest peasant was forced to buy expensive government salt when he could easily make it from seawater.
* **The Logic:** Breaking the salt law would highlight the inhumane nature of British rule in a way every villager could understand.

---

## üö∂ 2. The Dandi March (Salt Satyagraha)

*The Spark*

* **The Ultimatum:** Before marching, Gandhi sent his famous **"11 Points Demand"** letter to Viceroy Lord Irwin. It included reducing land revenue, abolishing the salt tax, and releasing political prisoners. Irwin ignored it.
* **The Start:** On **March 12, 1930**, Gandhi set out from **Sabarmati Ashram** (Ahmedabad) with **78 trusted volunteers**.
* **The Journey:** They walked **240 miles** (385 km) to the coastal village of **Dandi**.
* Thousands joined him along the way. The path became a pilgrimage of freedom.
* Gandhi was 61 years old but walked faster than the young men.


* **The Climax:** On **April 6, 1930**, Gandhi reached the Dandi coast, picked up a handful of salt, and formally broke the Salt Law.

---

## üåä 3. The Spread of the Movement

Once the signal was given at Dandi, the movement exploded across India.

* **Tamil Nadu:** **C. Rajagopalachari** led a march from Trichy to Vedaranyam.
* **Malabar (Kerala):** **K. Kelappan** walked from Calicut to Payyanur.
* **North-West Frontier Province (Peshawar):** **Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan** (the "Frontier Gandhi") led the **Red Shirts** (*Khudai Khidmatgars*).
* *Heroism:* The Garhwal Rifles (Hindu soldiers) refused to fire on the unarmed Muslim crowds here.


* **Dharasana Salt Works:**
* After Gandhi was arrested (May 1930), **Sarojini Naidu**, Imam Saheb, and Manilal Gandhi led a raid on the Dharasana Salt Works.
* *Brutality:* Police beat the non-violent protesters with steel-tipped lathis. American journalist **Webb Miller** reported: *"In 18 years of reporting... I have never witnessed such harrowing scenes as at Dharasana."*



---

## ‚úä 4. Forms of Protest

Civil Disobedience was different from Non-Cooperation. In 1920, they refused to *cooperate*; in 1930, they willfully *broke the law*.

1. **Breaking Laws:** Manufacturing salt, violating forest laws (Forest Satyagraha in Maharashtra/Karnataka).
2. **No Tax Campaign:** Peasants in Gujarat (Bardoli) and UP refused to pay revenue.
3. **Women's Participation:** This was the breakthrough feature. Women picketed liquor shops and foreign cloth shops in thousands.
4. **Prabhat Pheris:** Morning processions singing patriotic songs kept the spirit alive.
5. **Vanar Senas:** Children organized into "Monkey Brigades" to distribute leaflets and messages.

---

## üõë 5. The Truce: Gandhi-Irwin Pact (1931)

The government realized repression wasn't working. 90,000 people were in jail, but the movement continued.

* **First Round Table Conference (1930):** Held in London. The Congress boycotted it. The British realized talking about India's future without the Congress was like "Hamlet without the Prince of Denmark."
* **The Pact (March 5, 1931):** Gandhi and Lord Irwin signed a truce.
* **Government Agreed:** To release political prisoners (except those involved in violence, like Bhagat Singh), allow making salt for personal use, and return confiscated land.
* **Congress Agreed:** To suspend the Civil Disobedience Movement and participate in the **Second Round Table Conference**.



### üìâ The Criticism

Gandhi was heavily criticized by the youth (and Leftists) for **not saving Bhagat Singh, Sukhdev, and Rajguru**, who were hanged just days later (March 23, 1931).

---

## üìâ 6. Failure & Renewal

* **Second Round Table Conference (London, 1931):** Gandhi went as the sole representative of Congress. The talks failed because the British focused on communal questions (separate electorates for Untouchables) rather than independence.
* **Renewal (1932):** Gandhi returned empty-handed and restarted the movement.
* **The End:** The new Viceroy, **Lord Willingdon**, unleashed brutal repression. The movement slowly lost momentum and was officially withdrawn in **1934**.

### üìù Significance

Though it didn't win independence immediately, it won the moral victory. It proved that the British survived only by force, not consent.

### üöÄ Next Step

While Gandhi was in London, the British Prime Minister announced the "Communal Award," threatening to split the Hindu society forever.


---
a detailed breakdown of the **Communal Award** and the **Poona Pact (1932)**, a dramatic political standoff that redefined the social and political structure of India.

---

# ‚ö° The Communal Award & Poona Pact (1932)

*The Battle for the Soul of Hindu Society*

> *"I might not object to separate electorates for the Muslims and the Sikhs... but I will resist with my life the separation of the Untouchables from the Hindu fold."* ‚Äî **Mahatma Gandhi**

### 1. The Context: Failure of Talks

At the **Second Round Table Conference (1931)** in London, the talks failed because Dr. B.R. Ambedkar demanded **Separate Electorates** for the "Depressed Classes" (Untouchables), arguing that upper-caste Hindus would never represent their interests. Gandhi vehemently opposed this, fearing it would permanently split the Hindu society.

### 2. The Communal Award (August 16, 1932)

*The British Trap*

British Prime Minister **Ramsay MacDonald** announced the "Communal Award."

* **The Provision:** It extended the system of **Separate Electorates** not just to Muslims, Sikhs, and Christians, but now also to the **Depressed Classes** (Dalits).
* **What it meant:** In a separate electorate, only a Dalit could vote for a Dalit candidate. This legally recognized Dalits as a distinct minority separate from the Hindu religion (like Muslims).
* **British Motive:** To weaken the National Movement by dividing the majority Hindu community ("Divide and Rule" at its peak).

### 3. Gandhi‚Äôs Reaction: The Fast unto Death

Gandhi, then imprisoned in **Yerwada Jail (Pune)**, saw this as a lethal blow to Indian unity.

* **His Logic:** If Dalits were separated politically, the social reform movement to remove Untouchability would die. They would become a permanent separate interest group rather than being integrated into society.
* **The Action:** On **September 20, 1932**, Gandhi began a **Fast unto Death**.
* **National Panic:** The nation was stunned. Temples were thrown open to Dalits; mass prayers were held. The pressure mounted on Dr. Ambedkar to save Gandhi‚Äôs life.

### 4. The Moral Dilemma: Ambedkar vs. Gandhi

This was a clash of two titans with different visions for the same oppressed group:

* **Ambedkar's View:** Political power is the only key to social upliftment. We cannot trust the "Mahatma" or the upper castes; we need legal guarantees.
* **Gandhi's View:** Untouchability is a sin of Hinduism that Hindus must correct. Separating Dalits will only lead to bloodshed and permanent alienation.

### 5. The Compromise: The Poona Pact (September 24, 1932)

Under immense public pressure, Dr. Ambedkar agreed to negotiate. He met Gandhi in Yerwada Jail. The result was the **Poona Pact**, signed on behalf of Gandhi by **Madan Mohan Malaviya** and others.

#### **Key Terms of the Pact:**

1. **No Separate Electorates:** The idea of a separate electorate for Depressed Classes was abandoned.
2. **Joint Electorates:** All Hindus would vote together.
3. **Increased Reserved Seats:** In return, Ambedkar secured **more seats** than the British had offered.
* *Communal Award Offer:* 71 Seats.
* *Poona Pact Settlement:* **147 Seats** (in Provincial Legislatures) and **18%** of the total seats in the Central Legislature.



### 6. Significance & Aftermath

* **Victory for Both:** Gandhi saved the unity of Hindu society; Ambedkar secured a massive political voice for the Dalits (which continues today as "Reserved Constituencies").
* **Shift in Focus:** After the pact, Gandhi retired from active politics for a while to focus entirely on **"Harijan"** (Children of God) welfare.
* He started the **Harijan Sevak Sangh** (1932).
* He started the weekly journal *Harijan*.
* He conducted a nationwide "Harijan Tour" to collect funds and open wells/temples for Dalits.



### üìù Summary Table

| Feature | **Communal Award (British Plan)** | **Poona Pact (Indian Solution)** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Electorate Type** | **Separate** (Only Dalits vote for Dalits). | **Joint** (Everyone votes, but seat is reserved). |
| **Status of Dalits** | Distinct minority outside Hinduism. | Part of Hindu society. |
| **Seats Reserved** | **71** | **147** (More than double). |

### üöÄ Next Step

The constitutional framework is evolving. The British eventually codified these changes in the massive **Government of India Act 1935**, which serves as the blueprint for India's current Constitution.

---
a detailed breakdown of the **Government of India Act 1935** (the blueprint of India‚Äôs current Constitution) and the **1937 Elections** (Congress's first taste of power).

---

# üìú Part 1: The Government of India Act, 1935

*The "Slave Constitution" or The Blueprint?*

> *"A machine with strong brakes but no engine."* ‚Äî **Jawaharlal Nehru**
> *"Thoroughly rotten, fundamentally bad, and totally unacceptable."* ‚Äî **M.A. Jinnah**

After three Round Table Conferences and a "White Paper," the British Parliament passed its longest-ever Act. It was a masterpiece of legal drafting but a disaster of political intent.

### 1. Key Features of the Act

The Act was huge (321 Sections, 10 Schedules). It laid the structural foundation for modern India.

#### **A. All India Federation (The Failed Dream)**

* **Proposal:** A Federation comprising British Indian Provinces and the Princely States.
* **Condition:** It would only come into existence if 50% of the Princely States joined.
* **Result:** The Princes refused to join (fearing loss of power). Thus, the Federation **never came into existence**, and the Central Government continued under the 1919 Act structure.

#### **B. Provincial Autonomy (The Real Change)**

* **End of Dyarchy:** The hated "Dyarchy" system (introduced in 1919) was abolished in the provinces.
* **Autonomy:** Provinces were given an independent legal status. They were no longer just agents of the Center.
* **Responsible Government:** The Governor was required to act with the advice of Ministers responsible to the provincial legislature.
* **However:** The Governor retained "Special Powers" (discretionary powers) to veto bills or take over administration.

#### **C. Dyarchy at the Center**

* While Dyarchy was removed from provinces, it was introduced at the Center.
* **Reserved Subjects:** Defense and Foreign Affairs were reserved for the Viceroy.
* **Transferred Subjects:** Other departments were given to Indian ministers.

#### **D. Other Major Provisions**

* **Separation of Burma:** Burma (Myanmar) was separated from India.
* **New Provinces:** Sindh was separated from Bombay; Orissa was separated from Bihar.
* **Federal Court:** Established in Delhi (1937) to settle disputes between Center and Provinces (Precursor to the Supreme Court).
* **RBI:** It paved the way for the establishment of the **Reserve Bank of India**.

---

# üó≥Ô∏è Part 2: The Provincial Elections of 1937

*The Congress Sweeps In*

Despite calling the Act "slave-like," the Congress decided to contest the elections to:

1. Prove its popularity.
2. "Wreck the Act from within" (prevent non-Congress elements from capturing power).

### 1. The Results (The Congress Hurricane)

The elections were held in early 1937. The results shocked the British.

| Region | Result |
| --- | --- |
| **Madras, UP, Bihar, Central Provinces, Orissa** | **Clear Majority** for Congress. |
| **Bombay** | Near Majority (Congress formed government). |
| **NWFP & Assam** | Congress formed coalition governments later. |
| **Bengal** | Coalition of **Krishak Praja Party** (Fazlul Haq) and Muslim League. |
| **Punjab** | **Unionist Party** (Sikandar Hayat Khan) won. |
| **Sindh** | Local parties. |

**Summary:** Congress formed ministries in **8 out of 11 provinces**. The Muslim League performed poorly, failing to form a government even in Muslim-majority provinces (like Punjab and NWFP).

### 2. The 28-Month Rule of Congress (1937‚Äì1939)

For the first time, Indians were ruling Indians (at the provincial level).

#### **A. Achievements**

* **Civil Liberties:** Restrictions on the press were lifted. Political prisoners (including revolutionaries) were released. Police powers were curbed.
* **Agrarian Reforms:** Tenancy acts were passed to protect peasants from eviction. Rent was reduced in some areas.
* **Social Reforms:** Temple entry for Harijans was promoted. Prohibition (ban on alcohol) was introduced in Madras and Bombay.
* **Planning:** The **National Planning Committee** was set up in 1938 under **Jawaharlal Nehru** (by Congress President Subhash Chandra Bose).

#### **B. Limitations**

* They could not implement radical land reforms (like abolishing Zamindari) because the Ministries had limited powers and feared losing the support of landlord allies.
* They had to work under the strict financial control of the British Governors.

### 3. The Resignation (November 1939)

The dream run ended abruptly.

* **The Cause:** **World War II** broke out in September 1939. Viceroy **Lord Linlithgow** declared India a participant in the war **without consulting** the Indian leaders.
* **The Protest:** The Congress argued: *"How can a purely enslaved nation fight for the freedom of others?"*
* **The Action:** All Congress Ministries **resigned** in protest in October‚ÄìNovember 1939.
* **Jinnah's Reaction:** The Muslim League celebrated December 22, 1939, as **"Day of Deliverance"** (deliverance from "Congress Hindu Rule").

---

### üìù Summary of Significance

The 1935 Act and 1937 Elections proved two things:

1. **Congress was the dominant force** in India.
2. **Communalism was rising:** The Muslim League, stung by its defeat, began an aggressive campaign claiming "Islam is in Danger" under Congress rule, which eventually led to the demand for Pakistan.

### üöÄ Next Step

The war has started. The political deadlock is back.

---
 detailed breakdown of **Nationalism during World War II**, covering the "August Offer," "Individual Satyagraha," and the climactic "Quit India Movement."

---

# üåç Nationalism during WWII (1939‚Äì1942)

*The Final Showdown*

> *"Here is a mantra, a short one, that I give you... The mantra is: 'Do or Die'. We shall either free India or die in the attempt."* ‚Äî **Mahatma Gandhi**

When World War II began (1939), the Congress resigned from provincial ministries because India was dragged into the war without consent. The British, desperate for Indian cooperation against the Nazis and Japan, made a series of offers.

---

## üìú 1. The August Offer (1940)

*The First Olive Branch*

Viceroy **Lord Linlithgow** made a proposal on **August 8, 1940**, to win over the Congress.

* **The Offer:**
* **Dominion Status** as the long-term objective.
* Expansion of the Viceroy‚Äôs Executive Council to include more Indians.
* A constituent assembly *after the war* to frame the constitution.


* **The Rejection:**
* **Congress:** Rejected it because they demanded "Complete Independence," not Dominion Status. Nehru said, *"Dominion status concept is dead as a doornail."*
* **Muslim League:** Rejected it because it didn't explicitly promise Pakistan (though it gave them a veto power).



---

## üö∂ 2. Individual Satyagraha (1940‚Äì41)

*The Symbolic Protest*

Gandhi didn't want to embarrass the British during the war (who were fighting Hitler), but he couldn't remain silent either. He chose a middle path: **Individual Satyagraha**.

* **The Goal:** To affirm the **Right to Speech**. The Satyagrahi would simply make an anti-war speech and court arrest, showing that India was not voluntarily in the war.
* **The Satyagrahis:**
1. **First Satyagrahi:** **Acharya Vinoba Bhave** (started at Paunar Ashram).
2. **Second Satyagrahi:** **Jawaharlal Nehru**.
3. **Third Satyagrahi:** **Brahma Datt**.


* **Result:** About 25,000 people were arrested. It kept political interest alive without causing chaos.

---

## ‚úàÔ∏è 3. The Cripps Mission (March 1942)

*The "Post-Dated Cheque"*

By 1942, Japan had conquered Singapore and Rangoon and was knocking on India‚Äôs doors. Under pressure from the USA and China, British PM Winston Churchill sent **Sir Stafford Cripps** to India.

* **The Proposal:**
* **Dominion Status** with the right to secede from the Commonwealth.
* A Constituent Assembly after the war.
* **Right to Secede:** Any province that didn't like the new constitution could leave the Union (A blueprint for Pakistan).


* **Why it Failed:**
* It offered nothing *immediate* (real power remained with the Viceroy).
* Gandhi famously called it **"A post-dated cheque on a crashing bank."**
* The Congress rejected the "Right to Secede" clause.



---

## üî• 4. The Quit India Movement (August 1942)

*The Leaderless Revolt*

The failure of the Cripps Mission convinced Gandhi that the British would never leave voluntarily. He decided to launch his last and biggest struggle.

### **A. The Resolution (August 8, 1942)**

* **Venue:** Gowalia Tank Maidan, Bombay (now August Kranti Maidan).
* **The Demand:** An immediate end to British Rule.
* **The Slogan:** **"Do or Die"** (*Karo ya Maro*).
* **Gandhi‚Äôs Instructions:**
* *Government Servants:* Don't resign, but declare allegiance to Congress.
* *Soldiers:* Don't leave the army, but refuse to fire on Indians.
* *Students:* Leave studies if confident.
* *Peasants:* Refuse to pay taxes.



### **B. The Crackdown (August 9, 1942)**

* **Operation Zero Hour:** Before the movement could officially start, the British arrested **all top leaders** (Gandhi, Nehru, Patel, Azad) overnight.
* **Gandhi:** Imprisoned in **Aga Khan Palace** (Pune).
* **Others:** Sent to Ahmednagar Fort.

### **C. The Revolt (Power to the People)**

With no leaders to guide them, the people took over. It became violent and spontaneous.

* **Violence:** Police stations, railway tracks, and post offices were burnt. "The symbols of British authority were attacked."
* **Underground Radio:** **Usha Mehta** ran a secret "Congress Radio" to broadcast news.
* **Socialist Heroes:** **Jayaprakash Narayan (JP)** and **Aruna Asaf Ali** went underground to organize the resistance.

### **D. Parallel Governments (Sarkar)**

In some districts, British rule completely vanished, and locals set up their own governments:

1. **Ballia (UP):** Under **Chitu Pandey** (for one week).
2. **Tamluk (Bengal):** **Jatiya Sarkar**. (Famous for the 73-year-old **Matangini Hazra** who was shot holding the flag).
3. **Satara (Maharashtra):** **Prati Sarkar** (longest-lasting).

---

## üìâ 5. Suppression & Significance

The British used brutal force (machine guns from air) to crush the movement by end-1942. Over 10,000 were killed.

* **Did it fail?** Militarily, yes. But politically, it was a victory.
* **The Message:** It proved that the British could no longer rule India against the wishes of the people. The loyalty of the police and bureaucracy was shattered.
* **Viceroy‚Äôs Assessment:** Linlithgow described it as "the most serious rebellion since 1857."

### üöÄ Next Step

While the Congress was in jail, **Subhash Chandra Bose** was fighting the British from the outside with an army.

---
a detailed breakdown of the **Indian National Army (INA)** and the legendary saga of **Subhash Chandra Bose**, the man who decided to pay for freedom with blood.

---

# üêÖ Subhash Chandra Bose & The INA

*The War from Outside*

> *"Give me blood, and I will give you freedom!"* ‚Äî **Netaji Subhash Chandra Bose**

While Gandhi launched the "Quit India" movement inside the country, Subhash Chandra Bose (Netaji) launched a military invasion from the outside. He believed that non-violence alone was insufficient; India needed an army to kick the British out.

---

## üå©Ô∏è 1. The Rebel in the Congress (1938‚Äì1939)

Subhash was a brilliant leader (ICS rank 4, resigned) and a favorite of the youth. He was elected **Congress President** twice.

* **Haripura Session (1938):** Elected President unanimously. He set up the **National Planning Committee** (under Nehru) to plan India's industrial future.
* **Tripuri Session (1939) - The Crisis:**
* Bose wanted to re-contest. Gandhi opposed him and backed **Pattabhi Sitaramayya**.
* **The Result:** Bose won (1580 vs 1377 votes), defeating Gandhi's candidate.
* **The Fallout:** Gandhi declared, *"Pattabhi's defeat is my defeat."* The Congress Working Committee resigned in protest.
* **Resignation:** Unable to function without Gandhi's support, Bose resigned and formed the **Forward Bloc** (a radical party within Congress) to unite left-wing elements.



---

## üïµÔ∏è 2. The Great Escape (1941)

When WWII started, the British put Bose under house arrest in Calcutta.

* **The Plan:** On **January 16, 1941**, Bose escaped in the middle of the night dressed as a Muslim insurance agent named **"Ziauddin."**
* **The Journey:** He traveled from Calcutta  Peshawar  Kabul  Moscow  **Berlin (Germany)**.
* **In Germany:** He met **Hitler**, founded the *Free India Center*, and started the *Azad Hind Radio*. The title **"Netaji"** was given to him by Indian soldiers in Germany.

---

## ‚öîÔ∏è 3. The Birth of the INA (Azad Hind Fauj)

The INA was not created by Bose initially.

* **Mohan Singh's Role:** After Japan defeated the British in Southeast Asia (Singapore/Malaya), thousands of Indian soldiers (POWs) were captured. **Captain Mohan Singh** organized them into an army to fight for India's freedom.
* **Rash Behari Bose:** An old revolutionary living in exile in Japan, he invited Subhash to take charge.

### **Bose Takes Charge (Singapore, 1943)**

* Subhash arrived in Singapore in July 1943.
* **Provisional Government:** On **October 21, 1943**, he formed the **Provisional Government of Free India** (*Arzi Hukumat-e-Azad Hind*).
* It was recognized by Germany, Japan, Italy, and 6 other nations.
* It declared war on Britain and the USA.


* **The Army:** The INA had 3 fighting brigades named after Congress leaders: **Gandhi**, **Nehru**, and **Azad**.
* **Rani of Jhansi Regiment:** An all-women combat unit led by **Captain Lakshmi Sahgal**. (A revolutionary concept at the time).

---

## üî´ 4. The Campaign: "Chalo Dilli" (1944)

* **The Motto:** *"Ittehad, Itmad, Qurbani"* (Unity, Faith, Sacrifice).
* **The Greeting:** *"Jai Hind"* (Victory to India).
* **The Advance:** The INA marched with the Japanese Army through Burma towards the Indian border.
* **The Victory:** On **April 14, 1944**, Colonel Shaukat Malik hoisted the Tricolour at **Moirang (Manipur)**. It was the first time the Indian flag flew on liberated Indian soil.
* **The Defeat:** The **Battle of Kohima** and **Imphal** proved disastrous. The monsoon ruined supply lines, and the Japanese retreated. The INA soldiers died in thousands due to hunger and malaria.

---

## ‚úàÔ∏è 5. The End & The Mystery

* **The Crash:** On **August 18, 1945** (days after Japan surrendered), Bose reportedly died in a plane crash in **Taihoku (Taipei)** while en route to Tokyo/Russia.
* **The Legacy:** His death remains a subject of controversy, but his life became a legend.

---

## ‚öñÔ∏è 6. The Red Fort Trials (1945‚Äì46)

*The Defeat that Won the War*

Ironically, the INA achieved more *after* its defeat than during the war. The British made a fatal mistake: they decided to publicly try the INA commanders for treason at the **Red Fort (Delhi)**.

* **The Accused (The Three Heroes):**
1. **Prem Kumar Sahgal** (Hindu)
2. **Shah Nawaz Khan** (Muslim)
3. **Gurbaksh Singh Dhillon** (Sikh)


* *Significance:* The British unintentionally united the three major communities of India in the dock.


* **The Defense:** The Congress set aside differences. **Bhulabhai Desai**, **Tej Bahadur Sapru**, and even **Jawaharlal Nehru** (wearing his lawyer‚Äôs robe after 25 years) defended them.
* **The Public Reaction:** The slogan *"Lal Qile se aayi aawaz, Sahgal, Dhillon, Shah Nawaz!"* echoed across India. Riots broke out.
* **The Verdict:** They were found guilty but **released** immediately due to fear of a mass military revolt.

---

## ‚öì 7. The Royal Indian Navy (RIN) Mutiny (1946)

Inspired by the INA trials, the Indian armed forces (the pillar of British rule) turned against their masters.

* **The Spark:** On **February 18, 1946**, ratings (sailors) on the ship **HMIS Talwar** in Bombay went on strike over bad food and racial abuse.
* **The Spread:** It spread to 78 ships and 20 shore establishments. Sailors hoisted the flags of Congress, Muslim League, and the Communist Party on the ships' masts.
* **Impact:** This was the final nail in the coffin. The British realized they could no longer rely on the Indian Army/Navy to hold India.

### üìù Summary

Netaji failed to capture Delhi militarily, but his ghost destroyed the loyalty of the British Indian Army, making Independence inevitable.


---
**National Movement During World War II** (Phase 1), covering the initial reaction, the British **August Offer**, and Gandhi's strategic **Individual Satyagraha**.

---

# üåç National Movement During World War II (Phase I: 1939‚Äì1941)

*The War of Nerves*

When World War II broke out in **September 1939**, India was dragged into the conflict by Viceroy **Lord Linlithgow** without consulting a single Indian leader. This unilateral action triggered a constitutional crisis.

### 1. The Congress Stand

The Congress Working Committee (CWC) met at Wardha and clarified its position:

* **Anti-Fascist:** We condemn Hitler and Nazism.
* **Anti-Imperialist:** We cannot fight for the freedom of Poland or France while we are enslaved at home.
* **Condition:** India will support the war effort *only if* Britain promises immediate **Complete Independence** and establishes a National Government at the center.

### 2. The Resignation of Ministries (1939)

The Viceroy rejected the demands, offering only vague promises for the future.

* **Protest:** In **October‚ÄìNovember 1939**, the Congress Ministries in **8 provinces** resigned in protest.
* **Jinnah‚Äôs Reaction:** The Muslim League celebrated December 22, 1939, as the **"Day of Deliverance"** (from Congress rule).

---

# üìú Part 1: The August Offer (1940)

*Too Little, Too Late*

With the fall of France to the Nazis in mid-1940, Britain was in desperate straits and needed Indian cooperation. Lord Linlithgow made a fresh proposal on **August 8, 1940**.

### **A. The Terms**

1. **Dominion Status:** For the first time, "Dominion Status" was explicitly offered as the long-term goal for India.
2. **Executive Council:** Immediate expansion of the Viceroy‚Äôs Executive Council to include more Indians.
3. **Constituent Assembly:** After the war, a body mainly comprising Indians would frame the new Constitution.
4. **Veto Power to Minorities:** A crucial clause stating that no future constitution would be adopted without the consent of minorities (effectively giving the **Muslim League a veto** over India‚Äôs future).

### **B. The Rejection**

* **Congress:** Rejected it. Jawaharlal Nehru famously said, *"The concept of Dominion Status is dead as a doornail."* They wanted full independence.
* **Muslim League:** Rejected it (temporarily) because it did not clearly promise a separate state (Pakistan), though they liked the veto power.

---

# üö∂ Part 2: Individual Satyagraha (1940‚Äì1941)

*The Symbolic Protest*

After rejecting the August Offer, the Congress faced a dilemma. A mass movement (like 1920 or 1930) might hamper the British war effort against Fascism, which Gandhi did not want to do initially. However, silence would imply acceptance of British rule.

### **A. The Strategy**

Gandhi devised a unique form of protest: **Individual Satyagraha**.

* **Limited Scope:** Instead of millions marching, selected individuals would break the law.
* **The Act:** The Satyagrahi would make a public anti-war speech (asserting the **Right to Free Speech**) and court arrest.
* **The Aim:** To prove that Indian participation in the war was coerced, not voluntary, without causing mass chaos.

### **B. The Satyagrahis**

Gandhi personally selected the first few Satyagrahis to ensure discipline:

1. **First Satyagrahi:** **Acharya Vinoba Bhave**. He started the Satyagraha on October 17, 1940, at Paunar Ashram (Maharashtra).
2. **Second Satyagrahi:** **Jawaharlal Nehru**.
3. **Third Satyagrahi:** **Brahma Datt**.

### **C. The Movement Spreads (Delhi Chalo)**

* By mid-1941, over **25,000** people had been convicted.
* The Satyagrahis marched towards Delhi, coining the slogan **"Delhi Chalo"** (not to be confused with Bose's later INA slogan).

### **D. Suspension**

The movement was suspended in **December 1941** when:

1. Japan attacked Pearl Harbor and threatened India's borders.
2. The British government released the Congress leaders to negotiate (leading to the **Cripps Mission**).

---

### üìù Summary Comparison

| Feature | **August Offer (1940)** | **Individual Satyagraha (1940-41)** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Originator** | Viceroy Linlithgow (British) | Mahatma Gandhi (Congress) |
| **Core Proposal** | Dominion Status + Post-war Constitution | Right to Speech + Anti-war protest |
| **Significance** | Recognized minorities' veto; first offer of Dominion Status. | Kept nationalism alive without violent confrontation during war. |
| **Outcome** | Rejected by all parties. | 25,000 arrested; paved way for Cripps Mission. |

### üöÄ Next Step

The "Phony War" ended when Japan reached the doors of India in 1942.


---
 a detailed breakdown of the **Cripps Mission (1942)** and the decisive **Quit India Movement**, the final "Do or Die" battle for Indian independence.

---

# ‚úàÔ∏è Part 1: The Cripps Mission (March 1942)

*The "Post-Dated Cheque"*

By early 1942, the war situation was critical. Japan had conquered Singapore, Malaya, and Rangoon, and was knocking on India's doors. Under pressure from US President **Roosevelt** and Chinese President **Chiang Kai-shek** to get India's support, British PM Winston Churchill sent **Sir Stafford Cripps** (a Labour minister known to be friendly to India) with a proposal.

### 1. The Proposals

Cripps arrived in Delhi on March 23, 1942, with a draft declaration:

* **Dominion Status:** India would be a Dominion associated with the United Kingdom, with the right to secede from the Commonwealth.
* **Constituent Assembly:** After the war, a constitution-making body would be elected by provincial assemblies and nominated by princes.
* **The "Pakistan" Clause:** Any province that did not accept the new constitution would have the **right to secede** and form a separate union.
* **Immediate Power:** During the war, the British Viceroy would retain all real power, especially over **Defense**.

### 2. Why it Failed

Every political party rejected it for different reasons.

* **The Congress:**
* Rejected the **"Right to Secede"** for provinces (saw it as a blueprint for dividing India).
* Demanded full independence *now*, not vague promises for the future.
* **Gandhi's famous remark:** He reportedly called the offer **"A post-dated cheque on a crashing bank."**


* **The Muslim League:** Rejected it because it did not *explicitly* concede Pakistan (though it offered an escape route).
* **The Depressed Classes (Ambedkar):** Feared that an upper-caste dominated assembly would not protect their rights.

Result: Cripps returned home empty-handed in April 1942.

---

# üî• Part 2: The Quit India Movement (August 1942)

*The Leaderless Revolution*

> *"Here is a mantra... 'Do or Die'. We shall either free India or die in the attempt."* ‚Äî **Mahatma Gandhi**

The failure of the Cripps Mission convinced Gandhi that the British would never leave voluntarily. He felt that the British presence in India was actually *inviting* a Japanese invasion. To save India, the British had to go.

### 1. The Resolution

* **Wardha Meeting (July 1942):** The Congress Working Committee (CWC) accepted the idea of a struggle.
* **Bombay Session (August 8, 1942):** At the Gowalia Tank Maidan (now August Kranti Maidan), the historic **"Quit India Resolution"** was passed.
* **Demand:** Immediate end to British rule.
* **Leadership:** Gandhi was named the leader of the non-violent struggle.



### 2. Operation Zero Hour (August 9, 1942)

The British were prepared. Before the movement could officially start, they launched a pre-dawn crackdown.

* **Top Leaders Arrested:** Gandhi, Nehru, Patel, Azad, and virtually the entire Congress leadership were arrested overnight.
* **Gandhi:** Imprisoned in **Aga Khan Palace** (Pune) with his wife Kasturba (who died there) and secretary Mahadev Desai (who also died there).
* **Others:** Jailed in Ahmednagar Fort.

### 3. Phases of the Revolt

With no leaders to guide them, the people took charge.

**A. The Violent Outburst (August‚ÄìSeptember)**

* The news of the arrests angered the masses.
* **Symbols of Authority:** Police stations, post offices, railway tracks, and telegraph lines were destroyed across UP, Bihar, and Bengal.
* **Students and Workers:** Strikes in factories (Ahmedabad, Jamshedpur) and student walkouts became common.

**B. The Underground Movement**
Socialist leaders who evaded arrest went underground to coordinate the struggle.

* **Key Figures:** **Jayaprakash Narayan (JP)** (escaped from Hazaribagh Jail), **Ram Manohar Lohia**, and **Aruna Asaf Ali** (the "Heroine of 1942" who hoisted the flag at Gowalia Tank).
* **Congress Radio:** **Usha Mehta**, a 22-year-old student, ran a secret radio station to broadcast news and keep morale high until she was discovered.

**C. Parallel Governments (Jatiya Sarkar)**
In some districts, British rule completely collapsed, and locals set up their own administrations.

1. **Ballia (UP):** **Chitu Pandey** declared independence for a week. He released all prisoners from the jail.
2. **Tamluk (Bengal):** Set up the **"Tamralipta Jatiya Sarkar"** (lasted for two years!).
* *Heroism:* 73-year-old **Matangini Hazra** led a procession and was shot dead holding the tricolour, chanting "Vande Mataram."


3. **Satara (Maharashtra):** The **"Prati Sarkar"** led by **Nana Patil** set up "Nyayadan Mandals" (People's Courts) and punished pro-British elements.

### 4. Suppression

The British unleashed "white terror."

* Machine guns were used from low-flying aircraft against crowds.
* Over 10,000 people were killed in police firing.
* Villages were fined heavily.

### 5. Significance

* **The Final Blow:** It destroyed the loyalty of the bureaucracy and police. The British realized they could not hold India without the consent of the people.
* **New Leadership:** It brought a new generation of leaders (JP, Lohia, Chavan) to the forefront.
* **No Retreat:** After 1942, there was no going back. The only question left was *when* the British would leave, not *if*.

### üöÄ Next Step

The war ended in 1945, and the British Labour Party came to power, promising independence.


---
detailed notes on the **Growth of Communalism**, the later phase of **Peasant Movements** (20th Century), and the often-overlooked **State People‚Äôs Struggle** in the Princely States.

---

# ‚ò™Ô∏è 1. Growth of Communalism

*The Road to Partition*

Communalism in India was not a remnant of the medieval past but a modern colonial product. It evolved in three distinct stages.

### **Stage I: Liberal Communalism (Pre-1937)**

* **Nature:** Leaders believed that Hindus and Muslims had different interests, but these could be reconciled within one nation.
* **Key Players:** **Syed Ahmed Khan** (early phase), **Madan Mohan Malaviya**, **Lala Lajpat Rai**.
* **Demands:** Jobs, separate electorates, and reservations. It was basically a struggle for a share in the "middle-class pie."

### **Stage II: Extreme Communalism (1937‚Äì1940)**

* **Nature:** Believed that interests were not just different but *incompatible*. "If you gain, I lose."
* **Trigger:** The Congress victory in the **1937 Elections**. The Muslim League failed to form governments and felt isolated.
* **Propaganda:** The League launched a campaign alleging "Hindu Tyranny" under Congress rule. The **Pirpur Report** (1938) listed exaggerated atrocities against Muslims.
* **Jinnah‚Äôs Shift:** Jinnah declared that "democracy is not suited for India" because it means permanent Hindu majority rule.

### **Stage III: Separatist Communalism (Post-1940)**

* **Nature:** The "Two-Nation Theory." Hindus and Muslims are two separate nations and cannot coexist.
* **Lahore Resolution (1940):** The Muslim League officially demanded a separate state (Pakistan).
* **Direct Action Day (1946):** When the Cabinet Mission failed, Jinnah called for violence ("Direct Action") to achieve Pakistan, leading to the **Great Calcutta Killings**.

---

# üåæ 2. Peasant Movements (20th Century Phase)

*From Local Riots to Organized Unions*

Unlike the sporadic uprisings of the 19th century (Indigo/Santhal), the 20th-century peasant movements were highly organized, often led by Socialists and Communists, and linked to the National Freedom Struggle.

### **A. Formation of Kisan Sabhas**

* **The Pioneer:** **Swami Sahajanand Saraswati**.
* **All India Kisan Sabha (AIKS):** Founded in **Lucknow (1936)**.
* *President:* Swami Sahajanand.
* *Secretary:* N.G. Ranga.
* *Goal:* To fight against Zamindari oppression and demand land rights.



### **B. Key Movements**

| Movement | Region | Leader/Feature | Impact |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Eka (Unity) Movement (1921)** | UP (Awadh) | **Madari Pasi**. Peasants took religious oaths to pay only recorded rent and refuse forced labor. | Brutally suppressed by 1922. |
| **Bardoli Satyagraha (1928)** | Gujarat | **Sardar Patel**. Protest against 22% tax hike. | Success. Tax reduced to 6.03%. Patel got the title "Sardar" from the women of Bardoli. |
| **Tebhaga Movement (1946)** | Bengal | Led by **Communal Party**. Sharecroppers (*Bargadars*) demanded **2/3rd** of the harvest instead of 1/2. | "Tebhaga Chai" slogan. Laid basis for land reforms in West Bengal later. |
| **Telangana Movement (1946‚Äì51)** | Hyderabad | Armed revolt against the Nizam and feudal lords (*Deshmukhs*). | Biggest armed peasant struggle. Liberated 3000 villages. |

---

# üëë 3. State People‚Äôs Struggle (Prajamandal Movement)

*The Fight Against the Princes*

While the Congress fought the British in "British India," another struggle was brewing in the **562 Princely States** (ruled by Maharajas/Nawabs), which covered 40% of India.

### **A. The Condition**

* The Princes were protected by the British ("Paramountcy").
* Civil liberties were non-existent. No newspapers, no public meetings, no vote.
* Taxation was often higher than in British India to support the lavish lifestyles of the rulers.

### **B. The Prajamandals (People's Conferences)**

* People in states like Mysore, Hyderabad, Baroda, and Kashmir organized local bodies called **Prajamandals** to demand democratic rights and responsible government.
* **All India States People‚Äôs Conference (AISPC):** Formed in **1927** to coordinate these scattered struggles.
* **Jawaharlal Nehru** became its President in 1939, linking it firmly with the Congress.



### **C. The Congress Policy Shift**

* **Traditional Policy:** Non-interference. Gandhi believed the states were independent entities.
* **Haripura Session (1938):** Under **Subhash Chandra Bose**, the Congress declared that *Purna Swaraj* included independence for the Princely States too.
* **Quit India (1942):** Gandhi gave a specific call to the Princes: *"Renounce your connection with the British and accept the sovereignty of your own people."*

### **D. Major Flashpoints**

* **Kashmir:** **Sheikh Abdullah** led the "Quit Kashmir" movement against Maharaja Hari Singh.
* **Hyderabad:** The State Congress and Communists fought the Nizam's private militia (Razakars).
* **Travancore:** The Punnapra-Vayalar uprising (1946) against the Dewan, C.P. Ramaswamy Iyer, who wanted to keep Travancore independent.

### üöÄ Next Step

These struggles in the states made Sardar Patel's job of integration easier in 1947.


---
a comprehensive breakdown of the **Quit India Movement (1942)**, the final and most decisive mass struggle of the Indian freedom movement.

---

# üî• The Quit India Movement (August Kranti) - 1942

*The "Do or Die" Battle*

> *"I am not going to be satisfied with anything short of complete freedom... We shall either free India or die in the attempt."* ‚Äî **Mahatma Gandhi**

The Quit India Movement was a spontaneous, violent, and leaderless uprising that demonstrated the British could no longer rule India against its will.

---

## üßê I. Why was it launched? (The Causes)

1. **Failure of Cripps Mission (April 1942):** The British refused to offer immediate independence. Gandhi realized they had no intention of leaving voluntarily.
2. **Japanese Threat:** Japan was advancing rapidly through Southeast Asia. Gandhi believed that the British presence in India was an *invitation* for Japan to attack. He argued, *"Leave India to God. If that is too much, then leave her to anarchy."*
3. **Wartime Hardships:** High inflation, shortage of rice, and the "Scorched Earth" policy in Bengal (destroying boats/cycles to hinder Japanese advance) created immense anger among the people.

---

## üì¢ II. The Launch (August 8, 1942)

* **Venue:** Gowalia Tank Maidan, Bombay (now known as *August Kranti Maidan*).
* **The Resolution:** The All India Congress Committee (AICC) ratified the "Quit India" resolution.
* **Gandhi‚Äôs Speech:** He gave the famous mantra **"Do or Die"** (*Karo ya Maro*).
* **Specific Instructions:**
* *Government Servants:* Do not resign, but declare loyalty to the Congress.
* *Soldiers:* Do not leave the army, but refuse to fire on fellow Indians.
* *Peasants:* Refuse to pay taxes.
* *Students:* Leave studies only if you can remain firm till independence is won.



---

## ‚ö° III. Operation Zero Hour (The Crackdown)

The British government was ready. In the early hours of **August 9, 1942**, they launched "Operation Zero Hour."

* **Top Leadership Arrested:** Gandhi, Nehru, Patel, Azad, and Kripalani were arrested before sunrise.
* **Destinations:**
* Gandhi  **Aga Khan Palace** (Pune).
* Other leaders  **Ahmednagar Fort**.


* **Ban:** The Congress was declared an unlawful association.

---

## üåä IV. Phases of the Movement (The Upsurge)

With no leaders to guide them, the masses interpreted "Do or Die" in their own way. The movement had three distinct phases:

### **Phase 1: Urban Revolt (First Week)**

* Strikes, demonstrations, and hoisting of national flags in cities like Bombay, Calcutta, and Delhi.
* **Aruna Asaf Ali** (the "Grand Old Lady of Independence") heroically hoisted the tricolour at Gowalia Tank right after the arrests.

### **Phase 2: Countryside Rebellion (Mid-August)**

* The movement shifted to the villages.
* **Symbols of Authority Targeted:** Peasants attacked police stations, railway tracks, post offices, and telegraph lines ("The nervous system of British rule").
* **Sabotage:** Railway lines were uprooted in Bihar and Eastern UP to cut off military supplies.

### **Phase 3: Underground Activity (September onwards)**

* Since open protest was brutally crushed, younger leaders went underground to coordinate the resistance.
* **Key Leaders:** **Jayaprakash Narayan (JP)** (escaped from Hazaribagh Jail), **Ram Manohar Lohia**, **Achyut Patwardhan**.
* **Congress Radio:** **Usha Mehta** ran a secret radio station (42.34 meters band) to broadcast news and Gandhi‚Äôs messages.

---

## üèõÔ∏è V. Parallel Governments (Jatiya Sarkar)

In some areas, British authority completely vanished, and locals established their own governments.

1. **Ballia (UP):** Led by **Chitu Pandey**. He claimed to be the district magistrate and released all prisoners. (Lasted 1 week).
2. **Tamluk (Bengal):** The **Tamralipta Jatiya Sarkar**. It set up arbitration courts and an armed militia (*Vidyut Vahini*). It lasted for two years (until 1944).
3. **Satara (Maharashtra):** The **Prati Sarkar** led by **Nana Patil**. It ran "Nyayadan Mandals" (People's Courts) and punished pro-British informers.

---

## üõë VI. Who did NOT participate?

Not all Indians supported the movement.

* **Muslim League:** Jinnah asked Muslims to stay away, saying the movement was aimed at establishing "Hindu Raj." Their slogan was *"Divide and Quit."*
* **Communist Party of India (CPI):** Supported the British because the USSR (Russia) was an ally of Britain in WWII. They called it a "People's War."
* **Hindu Mahasabha:** Savarkar and Syama Prasad Mookerjee opposed the movement and continued to run coalition governments with the Muslim League in Bengal and Sindh.
* **Princely States:** The rulers supported the British, though the people of the states sympathized with the movement.

---

## üìâ VII. Suppression & Significance

* **Brutality:** The British used machine guns from the air (in Patna). Over 10,000 people were killed, and villages were fined collectively.
* **Why it Matters:**
1. **End of Fear:** It proved that the British could only rule India by force, not by consent.
2. **Loyalty Lost:** The bureaucracy and police were demoralized.
3. **Inevitable Freedom:** Although the movement was crushed militarily, the British realized that after the war, holding onto India would be impossible.



### üöÄ Next Step

The war ends in 1945. The British are exhausted.



---
detailed notes on the **Wavell Plan (1945)** and the **Cabinet Mission Plan (1946)**, the final two major British attempts to keep India united before Partition became inevitable.

---

# ü§ù Part 1: The Wavell Plan (Shimla Conference, 1945)

*The Last Chance for Unity?*

> *"The breakdown of the Shimla Conference cleared the way for Pakistan."*

By 1945, World War II was ending in Europe. The British government, under pressure to solve the Indian constitutional deadlock, sent Viceroy **Lord Wavell** with a new proposal.

### 1. The Proposal (The Wavell Plan)

The plan was designed to fully "Indianize" the Executive Council as an interim measure until a new constitution could be written.

* **New Executive Council:** All members would be Indian, except for the Viceroy and the Commander-in-Chief.
* **Parity:** There would be **equal representation** for "Caste Hindus" and "Muslims" in the council.
* **Defense:** Would remain with the British Commander-in-Chief.
* **External Affairs:** Would be transferred to an Indian member.

### 2. The Shimla Conference (June 1945)

Wavell invited 21 political leaders (including Gandhi, Jinnah, and Maulana Azad) to Shimla to discuss the plan.

* **The Deadlock:** The talks failed entirely over the issue of Muslim representation.
* **Jinnah's Demand:** He insisted that *all* Muslim members of the council must be nominated by the Muslim League. He refused to accept any Muslim nominated by the Congress (calling Congress a "Hindu party").
* **Congress Stand:** The Congress, led by **Maulana Abul Kalam Azad** (its President), rejected this. They argued that Congress was a secular, national party and had the right to nominate Muslim representatives (like Azad himself).


* **The Result:** Wavell, not wanting to alienate Jinnah, declared the conference a **failure**.
* **Significance:** This was a massive tactical victory for Jinnah. It effectively gave the Muslim League a **veto power** over any future constitutional progress.

---

# üó≥Ô∏è Interlude: The Elections of 1945‚Äì46

Between the Wavell Plan and the next mission, general elections were held in India. The results polarized the country completely.

* **Congress:** Swept the "General" seats (91% vote share).
* **Muslim League:** Swept the "Muslim" seats (winning all 30 seats in the Central Assembly and 442 out of 509 Muslim seats in provinces).
* **Conclusion:** The electorate had effectively divided the country before the politicians did. The League could now legitimately claim to be the *sole* spokesman of Indian Muslims.

---

# üèõÔ∏è Part 2: The Cabinet Mission Plan (1946)

*The Final Blueprint for a United India*

In 1946, the new British Labour Government (PM Clement Attlee) sent a high-powered mission to India to find a way to transfer power peacefully.

* **Members:**
1. **Pethick Lawrence** (Secretary of State)
2. **Stafford Cripps** (President of Board of Trade)
3. **A.V. Alexander** (First Lord of Admiralty)



### 1. The Proposal (The Three-Tier Federation)

The Mission **rejected the demand for a sovereign Pakistan** (arguing it would entail partition of Punjab/Bengal and cause economic ruin). Instead, they proposed a complex federal structure to satisfy Jinnah's demand for autonomy within a united India.

* **Tier 1 (Union Center):** A weak central government controlling only **Defense, Foreign Affairs, and Communications**.
* **Tier 2 (Groups):** Provinces would be divided into three groups:
* **Group A:** Hindu-majority provinces (Madras, Bombay, UP, Bihar, etc.).
* **Group B:** Muslim-majority provinces in the North-West (Punjab, Sindh, NWFP, Baluchistan).
* **Group C:** Muslim-majority provinces in the East (Bengal, Assam).


* **Tier 3 (Provinces):** Full autonomy and residual powers.

### 2. The Acceptance (The Confusion)

Initially, both sides accepted the plan, but with conflicting interpretations.

* **Muslim League:** Accepted it (June 6) because they saw the "Grouping" clause (Groups B and C) as a stepping stone to Pakistan. They believed the grouping was *compulsory*.
* **Congress:** Accepted it (June 24) but interpreted that grouping was *optional* (specifically, they didn't want Assam forced into Group C with Bengal).

### 3. The Collapse

* **Nehru's Statement (July 10, 1946):** After becoming Congress President, Jawaharlal Nehru told the press that the Congress would enter the Constituent Assembly "unbound by agreements" and implying they could change the grouping arrangement.
* **Jinnah's Reaction:** Jinnah felt betrayed. He argued that if Congress could change the rules *after* the British left, Muslims would be permanently subjugated.
* **Withdrawal:** On **July 29, 1946**, the Muslim League withdrew its acceptance of the Cabinet Mission Plan.

---

# ‚öîÔ∏è Part 3: Direct Action Day (August 16, 1946)

*The Beginning of the End*

After rejecting the plan, Jinnah famously declared: *"We shall have India divided or we shall have India destroyed."*

* **The Call:** The League announced **August 16** as "Direct Action Day" to win Pakistan by force.
* **The Result:** The **Great Calcutta Killings**. Within 72 hours, over 4,000 people were killed and 100,000 left homeless in Calcutta.
* **Ripple Effect:** The riots spread to **Noakhali** (Bengal), **Bihar**, **Garhmukteshwar** (UP), and eventually **Punjab**. The dream of a united India drowned in blood.

### üöÄ Next Step

The British realized they had to leave immediately before the army collapsed or a full-scale civil war consumed them.

---

detailed notes on the **Mountbatten Plan (June 3 Plan)** and the **Indian Independence Act (1947)**, the legal instruments that birthed two new nations and ended 200 years of British rule.

---

# ‚öîÔ∏è Part 1: The Mountbatten Plan (June 3, 1947)

*The Surgery to Separate Conjoined Twins*

> *"The alternative to Partition is anarchy."* ‚Äî **Sardar Patel**

By early 1947, India was on the brink of civil war. The British Prime Minister **Clement Attlee** made a historic announcement on **February 20, 1947**: The British would leave India no later than **June 1948**, and **Lord Mountbatten** would replace Wavell as the new Viceroy to oversee the transfer.

### 1. The Situation

Mountbatten arrived in March 1947. He realized two things quickly:

1. The Cabinet Mission Plan (United India) was dead.
2. The communal violence was spreading so fast that waiting until June 1948 would mean leaving behind a graveyard. He advanced the date to **August 1947**.

### 2. The Plan (The "Dickie Bird Plan" / June 3 Plan)

Mountbatten presented his plan to the "Big Seven" leaders (Nehru, Patel, Kripalani, Jinnah, Liaquat, Nishtar, and Baldev Singh).

* **Partition:** India would be divided into two dominions: **India** and **Pakistan**.
* **Bengal & Punjab:** The legislative assemblies of these two provinces would vote on whether to partition their provinces.
* *Result:* They voted to split. West Punjab and East Bengal went to Pakistan; East Punjab and West Bengal remained in India.


* **Referendum:**
* **NWFP (North-West Frontier Province):** A referendum would decide its fate. (Despite Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan's boycott, it voted for Pakistan).
* **Sylhet (Assam):** A referendum would decide if it joined East Bengal (Pakistan).


* **Princely States:** They were given the choice to join either India or Pakistan. Independence (staying alone) was *technically* an option but strongly discouraged by Mountbatten.
* **Boundary Commission:** A commission led by **Sir Cyril Radcliffe** would draw the actual border lines.

### 3. Acceptance

* **Congress:** Accepted it as a "necessary evil" to stop the bloodshed and establish a strong central state.
* **Muslim League:** Accepted it (though Jinnah was unhappy with the "moth-eaten" Pakistan without the full provinces of Bengal and Punjab).

---

# üìú Part 2: The Indian Independence Act, 1947

*The Birth Certificate*

Based on the Mountbatten Plan, the British Parliament passed this Act in record time (Royal Assent on July 18, 1947).

### **Key Provisions:**

1. **Two Dominions:** On **August 15, 1947**, two independent dominions, India and Pakistan, would be created.
2. **End of British Rule:** The British Government would have no responsibility for the governance of India or Pakistan after this date. The title "Emperor of India" was dropped from the Royal Titles.
3. **Constituent Assemblies:** The existing Constituent Assemblies would act as the **Parliament** and have full power to frame any constitution (including the power to repeal this very Act).
4. **Governor-General:** Each dominion would have a Governor-General.
* **India:** Requested **Lord Mountbatten** to stay on as the first Governor-General.
* **Pakistan:** **M.A. Jinnah** became the Governor-General.


5. **Lapse of Paramountcy:** British treaties with the Princely States would lapse. The states became legally independent but were expected to accede to one of the dominions.

---

# üïõ Part 3: The Midnight Hour (August 14‚Äì15, 1947)

*Tryst with Destiny*

> *"At the stroke of the midnight hour, when the world sleeps, India will awake to life and freedom."* ‚Äî **Jawaharlal Nehru**

### **The Celebration**

* On the night of **August 14**, the Constituent Assembly met in the Constitution Hall (Delhi).
* **Jawaharlal Nehru** delivered his famous **"Tryst with Destiny"** speech.
* As the clock struck 12:00, the Union Jack was lowered, and the **Tricolour** was hoisted.

### **The Tragedy**

While Delhi celebrated, the borders were burning.

* **Partition Violence:** The **Radcliffe Line** was announced on August 17 (two days late), causing mass confusion.
* **Migration:** The largest mass migration in human history began. **15 million people** crossed borders (Muslims to Pakistan, Hindus/Sikhs to India).
* **Death Toll:** Estimates range from **500,000 to 1 million** people killed in communal riots.
* **Gandhi's Absence:** The "Father of the Nation" was not at the celebrations. He was in **Calcutta** (Noakhali), fasting and spinning his charkha to stop Hindus and Muslims from killing each other.

---

### üìù Final Summary: The Cost of Freedom

| **Gain** | **Loss** |
| --- | --- |
| Sovereign Nation State | Division of the Subcontinent |
| Democracy & Constitution | 1 Million Lives Lost |
| End of Colonial Exploitation | Kashmir Issue (Conflict with Pakistan) |

### üöÄ Conclusion

The struggle that began in 1857 ended in 1947. The British Raj was gone. The task of building a modern nation had just begun.


---
a detailed breakdown of the **Nationalist Upsurge Post-World War II (1945‚Äì1947)** and the final painful chapter of **Independence with Partition**.

---

# üå©Ô∏è Part 1: The Post-War Upsurge (1945‚Äì1946)

*The Thunderstorm Before Freedom*

When World War II ended in 1945, the British expected gratitude; instead, they faced a volcano of anger. The fear of British authority had completely evaporated.

### **1. The INA Trials (The Red Fort Trials)**

* **The Event:** The British decided to publicly try the commanders of Subhash Chandra Bose‚Äôs **Indian National Army (INA)** for treason at the Red Fort.
* **The Accused:** A Hindu (**Prem Kumar Sahgal**), a Muslim (**Shah Nawaz Khan**), and a Sikh (**Gurbaksh Singh Dhillon**).
* **The Reaction:** The entire nation stood as one. The Congress, Muslim League, and Sikhs all supported the prisoners.
* **Slogan:** *"Lal Qile se aayi aawaz, Sahgal, Dhillon, Shah Nawaz!"*
* **Outcome:** The British court convicted them, but the Commander-in-Chief **remitted their sentences** fearing a military rebellion. It was a massive moral victory for India.



### **2. The Royal Indian Navy (RIN) Mutiny (Feb 1946)**

* **The Spark:** On February 18, 1946, ratings (sailors) on **HMIS Talwar** in Bombay struck work over bad food and racial abuse.
* **The Explosion:** The mutiny spread to **78 ships** and **20 shore establishments** from Karachi to Calcutta.
* **The Symbol:** Sailors tore down the Union Jack and hoisted the flags of the **Congress, Muslim League, and Communist Party** tied together on the masts.
* **Significance:** This was the "last straw." The British realized the Indian armed forces‚Äîthe tool used to suppress 1857 and 1942‚Äîcould no longer be trusted.

### **3. Popular Upsurges**

* **Workman Strikes:** Postal and telegraph workers, railwaymen, and police went on strike across India.
* **Peasant Revolts:** The **Tebhaga Movement** in Bengal (sharecroppers demanding 2/3rd share) and the **Telangana Movement** in Hyderabad (armed revolt against feudal lords) showed that the poor were ready to fight.

---

# ‚öîÔ∏è Part 2: The Road to Partition (1946‚Äì1947)

*The Failure of Unity*

### **1. The Cabinet Mission (1946)**

* **Goal:** To transfer power to a united India.
* **Plan:** A weak center (controlling only defense/foreign affairs) and strong provinces grouped into three sections (A, B, C).
* **Failure:** The Congress and Muslim League disagreed on the "Grouping Clause." Jinnah withdrew acceptance and called for **"Direct Action."**

### **2. Direct Action Day (Aug 16, 1946)**

* Jinnah declared: *"We shall have India divided or we shall have India destroyed."*
* **The Consequence:** The **Great Calcutta Killings** left over 4,000 dead in 72 hours. Communal riots spread like wildfire to Noakhali (Bengal) and Bihar.

### **3. The Interim Government (Sept 1946)**

* **Jawaharlal Nehru** formed the Interim Government.
* **The League's Sabotage:** The Muslim League joined later but only to obstruct work. **Liaquat Ali Khan** (Finance Member) blocked funding for Congress ministries, paralyzing the administration.

---

# ‚úÇÔ∏è Part 3: Independence with Partition (1947)

*The Surgery*

### **1. Attlee‚Äôs Announcement (Feb 20, 1947)**

British PM Clement Attlee declared a deadline: The British would leave India by **June 1948**, regardless of whether politicians agreed on a constitution.

### **2. The Mountbatten Plan (June 3 Plan)**

* **Lord Mountbatten** replaced Wavell to speed up the exit. He realized unity was impossible.
* **The Plan:**
* Immediate transfer of power (advanced to **August 1947**).
* Partition of India into two dominions: **India** and **Pakistan**.
* Partition of **Punjab** and **Bengal** based on religious demographics.
* A **Referendum** in NWFP and Sylhet.


* **Acceptance:** Congress accepted it to stop the civil war. Jinnah accepted it to get Pakistan.

### **3. The Indian Independence Act (July 1947)**

* Passed by the British Parliament, it legally created two independent nations.
* It abolished the title "Emperor of India" and ended British paramountcy over Princely States.

---

# üïõ Part 4: The Transfer of Power (August 14‚Äì15, 1947)

### **The Midnight Hour**

* **Pakistan:** Celebrated independence on **August 14**. Jinnah became its first Governor-General.
* **India:** At midnight on **August 15**, India awoke to freedom. Nehru delivered the *"Tryst with Destiny"* speech.

### **The Bloodbath**

* While leaders celebrated in Delhi, **Punjab** was burning.
* **Radcliffe Line:** The boundary award was announced on August 17 (2 days late), causing panic.
* **Migration:** **15 million people** crossed the border on foot, bullock carts, and trains.
* **Massacres:** 'Ghost trains' arrived full of corpses. Between **500,000 to 1 million people died**.

### **Gandhi‚Äôs Absence**

The man who led the movement was not in Delhi. Gandhi was in **Calcutta**, fasting to stop communal riots, mourning the partition of the land he tried to unite.

### üèÅ Summary Timeline

| Date | Event | Significance |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Nov 1945** | **INA Trials** | United the nation; demoralized the British Army. |
| **Feb 1946** | **RIN Mutiny** | Naval revolt; British decided to leave. |
| **Aug 1946** | **Direct Action Day** | Communal riots made partition inevitable. |
| **June 1947** | **Mountbatten Plan** | Official plan for Partition. |
| **Aug 15, 1947** | **Independence** | Birth of India & Pakistan. |

This concludes the saga of the Indian National Movement.

---
the comprehensive **Timeline of the Indian Freedom Struggle (1857‚Äì1947)**, covering all major political events and the passing of the titans who shaped the nation.

---

# üï∞Ô∏è Chronicle of Freedom: 1857‚Äì1947

### **I. The First Spark & The Awakening (1857‚Äì1904)**

* **1857:** **The Revolt of 1857** begins (Sepoy Mutiny).
* **1858:** **Queen‚Äôs Proclamation** (Transfer of power from East India Company to British Crown).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Rani Laxmibai** (died fighting in Gwalior).


* **1859:** **Indigo Revolt** in Bengal (Neel Darpan).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Tantia Tope** (executed).


* **1875:** Founding of **Arya Samaj** (Dayanand Saraswati) and **Theosophical Society**.
* **1878:** **Vernacular Press Act** & Arms Act passed by Lord Lytton.
* **1882:** **Hunter Commission** on Education.
* **1883:** **Ilbert Bill Controversy**.
* üè¥ *Death:* **Dayanand Saraswati**.


* **1885:** **Formation of Indian National Congress (INC)** in Bombay (A.O. Hume).
* **1893:** Swami Vivekananda at the Chicago Parliament of Religions.
* **1897:** Plague in Pune; Chapekar Brothers assassinate Rand.
* **1898:** üè¥ *Death:* **Sir Syed Ahmed Khan**.
* **1902:** üè¥ *Death:* **Swami Vivekananda**.
* **1904:** Indian Universities Act (curbing autonomy).

---

### **II. The Era of Storm & Stress (1905‚Äì1918)**

* **1905:** **Partition of Bengal** announced by Lord Curzon. **Swadeshi Movement** begins.
* **1906:** Formation of **Muslim League** in Dhaka.
* *Congress Session:* Goal declared as "Swaraj" (Self-rule like UK colonies).


* **1907:** **Surat Split** (Moderates vs. Extremists).
* **1908:** Execution of **Khudiram Bose** (Alipore Bomb Case). Tilak jailed for 6 years.
* **1909:** **Morley-Minto Reforms** (Separate Electorates for Muslims).
* **1911:** **Delhi Durbar**; Partition of Bengal annulled; Capital shifts from Calcutta to Delhi.
* **1913:** **Ghadar Party** formed in San Francisco.
* **1915:** **Return of Mahatma Gandhi** to India (Jan 9).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Gopal Krishna Gokhale** (Gandhi's Guru).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Pherozeshah Mehta**.


* **1916:** **Lucknow Pact** (Congress-League unity) & **Home Rule Leagues** launched.
* **1917:** **Champaran Satyagraha** (Gandhi's first success).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Dadabhai Naoroji** (The Grand Old Man of India).


* **1918:** **Ahmedabad Mill Strike** & **Kheda Satyagraha**. End of WWI.

---

### **III. The Gandhian Era: Non-Cooperation to Purna Swaraj (1919‚Äì1929)**

* **1919:** **Rowlatt Act** passed.
* **Jallianwala Bagh Massacre** (April 13).
* **Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms**.


* **1920:** **Khilafat & Non-Cooperation Movement** launched.
* üè¥ *Death:* **Bal Gangadhar Tilak** (Aug 1 - day movement started).


* **1922:** **Chauri Chaura Incident**. Gandhi withdraws movement.
* **1923:** Formation of **Swaraj Party** (C.R. Das & Motilal Nehru).
* **1924:** HRA formed (Revolutionary group).
* **1925:** **Kakori Train Action**.
* üè¥ *Death:* **C.R. Das** (Deshbandhu).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Surendranath Banerjee**.


* **1927:** **Simon Commission** appointed.
* Execution of **Ashfaqullah Khan** & **Ramprasad Bismil**.


* **1928:** **Nehru Report** (First Constitution draft).
* **Bardoli Satyagraha** (Sardar Patel).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Lala Lajpat Rai** (due to lathi charge injuries).


* **1929:** **Lahore Session**; **Purna Swaraj** Resolution passed.
* Bombing of Central Assembly (Bhagat Singh & Dutt).



---

### **IV. The Battle for Independence (1930‚Äì1942)**

* **1930:** **Civil Disobedience Movement** begins with **Dandi March**.
* First Round Table Conference (Boycotted by Congress).


* **1931:** **Gandhi-Irwin Pact**; Second Round Table Conference.
* üè¥ *Death:* **Motilal Nehru**.
* üè¥ *Death:* **Chandrashekhar Azad** (Alfred Park encounter).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Bhagat Singh, Sukhdev, Rajguru** (Hanged March 23).


* **1932:** **Communal Award** & **Poona Pact**.
* **1933:** üè¥ *Death:* **Annie Besant**.
* **1934:** Civil Disobedience withdrawn.
* üè¥ *Death:* **Surya Sen** (Masterda) - Hanged.


* **1935:** **Government of India Act** passed.
* **1937:** Provincial Elections (Congress wins 8 provinces).
* **1939:** World War II begins. Congress Ministries resign.
* **Subhash Chandra Bose** forms **Forward Bloc**.


* **1940:** **August Offer**; **Lahore Resolution** (Pakistan demand).
* **Individual Satyagraha** starts.
* Execution of **Udham Singh** (killed Dyer).


* **1941:** üè¥ *Death:* **Rabindranath Tagore**.
* Subhash Bose escapes India.


* **1942:** **Cripps Mission**.
* **Quit India Movement** (Do or Die).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Jamnalal Bajaj**.



---

### **V. The Final Countdown (1943‚Äì1947)**

* **1943:** Bose forms **Azad Hind Sarkar** (Provisional Govt) in Singapore.
* **1944:** **INA** reaches Indian soil (Moirang).
* üè¥ *Death:* **Kasturba Gandhi** (in prison).


* **1945:** **Shimla Conference** (Wavell Plan) fails.
* **INA Trials** at Red Fort begin.
* üè¥ *Death:* **Subhash Chandra Bose** (Reported plane crash, Aug 18).


* **1946:** **RIN Mutiny** (Naval Revolt).
* **Cabinet Mission Plan**.
* **Direct Action Day** (Aug 16) & Great Calcutta Killings.
* üè¥ *Death:* **Madan Mohan Malaviya**.


* **1947:**
* **Feb 20:** Attlee's Announcement (British to leave by June 1948).
* **June 3:** **Mountbatten Plan** (Partition announced).
* **July 18:** **Indian Independence Act** passed.
* **Aug 14:** Creation of **Pakistan**.
* **Aug 15:** Independence of **India**.



---

**Post-Script (Immediate Aftermath):**

* **Jan 1948:** Assassination of **Mahatma Gandhi**.
* **Sept 1948:** Death of **M.A. Jinnah**.
* **1950:** Death of **Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel**.


---
 a comprehensive overview of the **Indian Freedom Struggle**, broken down by its evolutionary stages and highlighting key contributions from every corner of the country.

---

# üáÆüá≥ The Saga of Independence (1857‚Äì1947)

The struggle for freedom was not a single event but a century-long process that evolved from isolated uprisings to a massive, unified national movement.

## üï∞Ô∏è Phase I: The First War of Independence (1857)

* **Nature:** It was a military mutiny that turned into a popular rebellion.
* **Centers:** Meerut, Delhi, Kanpur, Lucknow, Jhansi, and Arrah (Bihar).
* **Outcome:** Though crushed, it ended the East India Company's rule and transferred power to the British Crown (1858).
* **Key Figure:** **Mangal Pandey** (Barrackpore), **Rani Laxmibai** (Jhansi).

## üï∞Ô∏è Phase II: The Moderate Phase (1885‚Äì1905)

* **The Awakening:** The **Indian National Congress (INC)** was formed in **1885** by A.O. Hume.
* **Method:** "Prayer, Petition, and Protest." They believed in constitutional reforms and the British sense of justice.
* **Key Figures:** **Dadabhai Naoroji** (Grand Old Man of India), **Gopal Krishna Gokhale**, **W.C. Bonnerjee**.
* **Contribution:** They exposed the "Economic Drain" of India's wealth to Britain.

## üï∞Ô∏è Phase III: The Extremist & Swadeshi Phase (1905‚Äì1918)

* **Trigger:** The Partition of Bengal (1905).
* **Method:** **Swadeshi** (use Indian goods) and **Boycott** (burn British goods).
* **Leaders:** The Trio **Lal-Bal-Pal** (Lajpat Rai, Bal Gangadhar Tilak, Bipin Chandra Pal) and **Aurobindo Ghosh**.
* **Slogan:** *"Swaraj is my birthright and I shall have it"* (Tilak).

## üï∞Ô∏è Phase IV: The Gandhian Era (1919‚Äì1942)

* **Transformation:** Mahatma Gandhi turned the movement from an elite struggle into a mass movement involving peasants, workers, and women.
* **Major Movements:**
1. **Non-Cooperation Movement (1920):** Allied with the Khilafat movement; first mass resistance.
2. **Civil Disobedience Movement (1930):** Sparked by the **Dandi March** (Salt Satyagraha).
3. **Quit India Movement (1942):** The final "Do or Die" battle.



## üï∞Ô∏è Phase V: The Revolutionary Movement (Parallel Stream)

* **Ideology:** Belief in armed struggle and sacrifice to awaken the nation.
* **Two Waves:**
1. **1905‚Äì1915:** Khudiram Bose, Prafulla Chaki, Rasbehari Bose (Ghadar Movement).
2. **1920s:** Bhagat Singh, Chandrashekhar Azad, Surya Sen (Masterda).



---

# üó∫Ô∏è Regional Contributions: Heroes from Every Corner

The freedom struggle was not limited to Delhi or Bengal. Every region contributed unique leaders and movements.

### **1. North India**

* **Punjab:**
* **Lala Lajpat Rai:** Led the protest against the Simon Commission; died from police lathi blows.
* **Bhagat Singh, Sukhdev, Rajguru:** Icons of the revolutionary socialist movement.
* **Udham Singh:** Assassinated Michael O'Dwyer in London to avenge Jallianwala Bagh.


* **Uttar Pradesh (United Provinces):**
* **Chandra Shekhar Azad:** Kept the revolutionary fire alive in North India.
* **Jawaharlal Nehru:** The architect of modern India and key leader of the Congress.
* **Ram Prasad Bismil:** The hero of the Kakori conspiracy.
* **Rani Laxmibai:** (Jhansi) The icon of 1857.



### **2. East India**

* **Bengal:**
* **Subhash Chandra Bose:** Founded the **Indian National Army (INA)** to fight the British militarily.
* **Surya Sen (Masterda):** Led the daring **Chittagong Armoury Raid**.
* **Matangini Hazra:** A 73-year-old woman shot dead holding the flag during Quit India.


* **Bihar:**
* **Kunwar Singh:** At age 80, he led the 1857 revolt in Arrah.
* **Dr. Rajendra Prasad:** A pillar of the Gandhian movement and first President of India.


* **Odisha:**
* **Chakhi Khuntia:** Played a crucial role in 1857.
* **Laxman Nayak:** Tribal leader martyred during Quit India.


* **Jharkhand:**
* **Birsa Munda:** Led the Munda Rebellion (Ulgulan) against the British and landlords.



### **3. West India**

* **Maharashtra:**
* **Bal Gangadhar Tilak:** The "Father of Indian Unrest."
* **Vinayak Damodar Savarkar:** Revolutionary thinker and leader of Abhinav Bharat.
* **Jyotiba Phule:** Social reformer who fought caste discrimination (Satya Shodhak Samaj).


* **Gujarat:**
* **Mahatma Gandhi:** The Father of the Nation.
* **Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel:** The "Iron Man" who unified India; led the **Bardoli Satyagraha**.
* **Dadabhai Naoroji:** The first Indian elected to the British Parliament.



### **4. South India**

* **Tamil Nadu:**
* **C. Rajagopalachari (Rajaji):** Led the Salt March in the South (Vedaranyam) and was the first Indian Governor-General.
* **V.O. Chidambaram Pillai:** Started the first indigenous Indian shipping service to compete with the British.
* **Subramania Bharati:** The poet whose songs ignited patriotism.


* **Andhra Pradesh:**
* **Alluri Sitarama Raju:** Led the **Rampa Rebellion** of tribals against the British (inspiration for the movie *RRR*).
* **Pingali Venkayya:** Designed the Indian National Flag.


* **Kerala:**
* **Velu Thampi Dalawa:** Led a revolt against the British in Travancore way back in 1809.
* **K. Kelappan:** Known as the "Kerala Gandhi," led the Vaikom Satyagraha for temple entry.


* **Karnataka:**
* **Kittur Chennamma:** Queen of Kittur who led an armed rebellion against the British in 1824 (much before 1857).



### **5. North-East India**

* **Manipur/Nagaland:**
* **Rani Gaidinliu:** A Naga spiritual leader who fought the British at the age of 13. Nehru called her the "Daughter of the Hills."


* **Assam:**
* **Kanaklata Barua:** A 17-year-old girl shot dead while trying to hoist the national flag during Quit India.
* **Maniram Dewan:** Executed for his role in the 1857 revolt in Assam.



---

### üìù Summary Table of Movements

| Era | Movement | Nature | Key Leader |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **1905** | **Swadeshi** | Cultural/Economic | Lal-Bal-Pal |
| **1913** | **Ghadar** | Revolutionary (Global) | Lala Har Dayal |
| **1916** | **Home Rule** | Political Demand | Tilak & Annie Besant |
| **1920** | **Non-Cooperation** | Mass Boycott | Gandhi |
| **1930** | **Civil Disobedience** | Breaking Laws (Salt) | Gandhi |
| **1942** | **Quit India** | Leaderless Revolt | The Common People |
| **1943** | **INA (Azad Hind)** | Military Invasion | Subhash Chandra Bose |



---
